###begin article-title 0
Distinct Roles of Non-Canonical Poly(A) Polymerases in RNA Metabolism
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: SSP SV WK APG. Performed the experiments: SSP SV LS. Analyzed the data: SSP LS APG. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: TS DB WK APG. Wrote the paper: SSP SV WK APG.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 392 399 392 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 485 498 485 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 519 528 519 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 532 541 528 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 564 573 556 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 729 738 717 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 746 755 730 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 912 916 892 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 981 991 961 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4(DADA)</italic>
###xml 1059 1066 1039 1046 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1153 1160 1133 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1441 1445 1421 1425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1500 1504 1480 1484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1591 1595 1571 1575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1614 1618 1594 1598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 469 474 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 485 498 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Trf4p and Trf5p are non-canonical poly(A) polymerases and are part of the heteromeric protein complexes TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 that promote the degradation of aberrant and short-lived RNA substrates by interacting with the nuclear exosome. To assess the level of functional redundancy between the paralogous Trf4 and Trf5 proteins and to investigate the role of the Trf4-dependent polyadenylation in vivo, we used DNA microarrays to compare gene expression of the wild-type yeast strain of S. cerevisiae with either that of trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutant strains or the trf4Delta mutant expressing the polyadenylation-defective Trf4(DADA) protein. We found little overlap between the sets of transcripts with altered expression in the trf4Delta or the trf5Delta mutants, suggesting that Trf4p and Trf5p target distinct groups of RNAs for degradation. Surprisingly, most RNAs the expression of which was altered by the trf4 deletion were restored to wild-type levels by overexpression of TRF4(DADA), showing that the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p is dispensable in vivo. Apart from previously reported Trf4p and Trf5p target RNAs, this analysis along with in vivo cross-linking and RNA immunopurification-chip experiments revealed that both the TRAMP4 and the TRAMP5 complexes stimulate the degradation of spliced-out introns via a mechanism that is independent of the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p. In addition, we show that disruption of trf4 causes severe shortening of telomeres suggesting that TRF4 functions in the maintenance of telomere length. Finally, our study demonstrates that TRF4, the exosome, and TRF5 participate in antisense RNA-mediated regulation of genes involved in phosphate metabolism. In conclusion, our results suggest that paralogous TRAMP complexes have distinct RNA selectivities with functional implications in RNA surveillance as well as other RNA-related processes. This indicates widespread and integrative functions of TRAMP complexes for the coordination of different gene expression regulatory processes.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 294 307 294 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1105 1112 1105 1112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 288 293 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 294 307 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
The discovery that most regions of the genome are actively transcribed into non-coding RNAs has dramatically increased interest in their function and regulation. Recent data from us and others have shed light on the molecular machinery that promotes the decay of such transcripts. In the yeast S. cerevisiae, Trf4p and Trf5p are alternative subunits of the so-called TRAMP complex, which degrades aberrant and short-lived RNAs. They add short poly(A) tails to their substrate RNAs that function as landing pads for exonucleases mediating RNA decay. Although alternate compositions of TRAMP complexes exist, the RNA substrate specificities and the processes controlled by them have not been determined. Applying a genome-wide approach, we describe overlapping yet distinct functional implications of different TRAMP complexes, and we demonstrate strong connections between RNA quality control and other RNA-related processes such as telomer length maintenance. Moreover, our study shows that the degradation of specific target RNAs is not strictly dependent on the polyadenylation activity of Trf proteins in vivo. These results suggest novel and integrative functions of TRAMP complexes for RNA regulation.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Introduction
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 579 582 579 582 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 583 586 583 586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley1">[2]</xref>
Gene expression in eukaryotes depends on highly complex mechanisms for production of mature RNA molecules. Precursors of mRNAs, ribosomal RNAs (rRNAs), transfer RNAs (tRNAs), small nucleolar RNAs (snoRNAs), and small nuclear RNA (snRNAs) undergo stepwise processing and maturation, which includes 5'-capping, splicing, 3'-polyadenylation, endo- and exonucleolytic trimming, and base modifications. All these processes are error-prone and thus, RNA maturation has to be monitored by nuclear and cytoplasmic RNA quality control pathways to remove potentially harmful aberrant RNAs [1],[2].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 21 45 21 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 218 221 218 221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Hilleren1">[3]</xref>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Martin1">[10]</xref>
###xml 458 461 458 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 462 465 462 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 667 671 667 671 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Edmonds1">[11]</xref>
###xml 672 676 672 676 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-MinvielleSebastia1">[12]</xref>
###xml 846 849 846 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 850 853 850 853 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 15 20 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 21 45 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
In the budding yeast Saccharomyces cerevisiae, nuclear RNA surveillance is mediated by the combined action of the Trf4/5-Air1/2-Mtr4 (TRAMP) complex and the exosome that promote rapid degradation of nonfunctional RNAs [3]-[10]. The TRAMP complex consists of either one of the two paralogous non-canonical poly(A) polymerases Trf4p and Trf5p forming TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 complexes, respectively, the RNA binding proteins Air1 or Air2, and the RNA helicase Mtr4p [5]-[7]. In contrast to the canonical poly(A) polymerase Pap1p, which adds long poly(A) tails to the 3'-end of mRNAs that facilitates nuclear RNA export and increases the stability and translation of messages [11],[12], the Trf proteins add short poly(A) tails to their substrate RNAs, which is assumed to trigger efficient decay of the RNAs by recruitment of the nuclear exosome complex [5]-[7].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 127 128 127 128 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i</sub>
###xml 128 131 128 131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Met</sup>
###xml 133 136 133 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Kadaba1">[4]</xref>
###xml 462 465 462 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 467 470 467 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 471 474 471 474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Rougemaille1">[9]</xref>
###xml 476 480 476 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Kadaba2">[13]</xref>
###xml 481 485 481 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley2">[17]</xref>
###xml 821 824 821 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1001 1010 1001 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 1066 1069 1062 1065 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1308 1312 1304 1308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Neil1">[18]</xref>
###xml 1313 1317 1309 1313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 1462 1466 1458 1462 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Neil1">[18]</xref>
###xml 1467 1471 1463 1467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
Initially, Trf4 protein was identified as a key player in the surveillance and degradation of hypomodified initiator tRNA (tRNAiMet) [4]. Further studies revealed more widespread roles of TRAMP complexes to assist the exosome-mediated degradation and trimming of several types of non-coding RNAs (ncRNAs) including precursors of rRNAs, tRNAs, snoRNAs, snRNAs, and of aberrant pre-mRNAs that are defective in 3' end cleavage, splicing, or export to the cytoplasm [1], [6]-[9], [13]-[17]. Many of these RNA substrates are part of ribonucleoprotein (RNP) complexes and pre-ribosomes suggesting that most if not all newly synthesized nuclear RNPs are subject to quality control by TRAMP and the exosome. Another major class of potential RNA targets for TRAMP complexes are the so-called 'cryptic unstable transcripts' (CUTs) [7]. CUTs are small, capped and fairly unstable transcripts that are expressed at such low levels that they can only be readily detected in nuclear RNA degradation mutants such as rrp6Delta. Originally detected in some intergenic regions (IGRs) [7], the recent systematic exploration of CUTs by RNA sequencing and tiling arrays suggests the existence of hundreds of CUTs that preferentially originate from nucleosome-free 5' promotor regions, or from the 3'-ends of protein-coding genes [18],[19]. However, whether these CUTs have a biological role, or merely reflect transcriptional noise made from nucleosome-depleted regions is not known [18],[19].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 114 118 114 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 119 123 119 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wery1">[21]</xref>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano1">[22]</xref>
###xml 273 282 273 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 422 429 418 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NEL025c</italic>
###xml 562 569 558 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 569 572 565 568 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 573 577 569 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Egecioglu1">[15]</xref>
###xml 578 582 574 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 583 587 579 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley4">[23]</xref>
Most studies investigating the functions of TRAMP complexes focused on TRAMP4 and much less is known about TRAMP5 [20],[21]. Trf4p and Trf5p share 56% amino-acid sequence similarity and loss of both poly(A) polymerases is lethal [22]. The conditional depletion of Trf5p in trf4Delta mutant cells increases the steady-state levels of specific RNAs, such as the 3'-extended forms of U14 snoRNA, the 23S pre-rRNA and the CUT NEL025c that accumulate in either single mutant indicating that Trf4p and Trf5p have at least partially overlapping substrate specificities in vivo[7],[15],[20],[23].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 116 120 116 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">top1</italic>
###xml 241 245 241 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano2">[24]</xref>
###xml 249 261 249 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">top1 trf4-ts</italic>
###xml 421 425 421 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano1">[22]</xref>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano2">[24]</xref>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Edwards1">[26]</xref>
###xml 489 493 489 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 590 594 590 594 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano1">[22]</xref>
###xml 656 664 656 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 763 767 763 767 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano2">[24]</xref>
###xml 769 773 769 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Berretta1">[27]</xref>
###xml 774 778 774 778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Buhler2">[32]</xref>
###xml 962 966 962 966 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley4">[23]</xref>
###xml 656 664 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Besides RNA quality control and processing, Trf proteins may also participate in DNA-related processes. Originally, TRF4 was identified in a screen for mutations that are synthetically lethal with top1, which encodes the DNA topoisomerase I [24]. A top1 trf4-ts double mutant was defective in several mitotic events, such as sister chromatid cohesion, chromosome condensation at the rDNA loci, and chromosome segregation [22], [24]-[26]. These defects were suppressed by overexpression of TRF5 suggesting that both Trf4p and Trf5p have roles in DNA metabolism and heterochromatin formation [22]. Moreover, Trf4p as well as the orthologous protein Cid14 in S. pombe stimulate the RNA-mediated silencing of heterochromatic transcripts and control rDNA copy numbers [24], [27]-[32]. Hence, it was postulated that RNA-mediated recruitment of Trf4p and Trf5p may promote chromatin remodeling through regulation of histone modifying enzymes at specific chromatin loci [23].
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 556 562 556 562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">per se</italic>
###xml 761 770 761 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
Although the above mentioned studies revealed some substrates and functions for complexes containing Trf4 (TRAMP4) and Trf5 (TRAMP5), a comprehensive view of the substrate specificities and potential functional implications of the different TRAMP complexes is still lacking. We therefore wished to obtain a global picture of the RNA substrates that are regulated by the TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 complexes. To this end, we have used DNA microarrays to systematically map the RNA targets of Trf4p and Trf5. Surprisingly, we found that the different TRAMP complexes per se regulate only marginally overlapping sets of RNAs in the cell. Furthermore, the polyadenylation-defective form of Trf4p (Trf4p-DADA) suppressed most of the altered expression pattern as seen in the trf4Delta mutant cells suggesting that the TRAMP polyadenylation activity is not essential for RNA regulation. We further demonstrate that Trf4p and to a lower extent Trf5p promotes the degradation of a group of introns through an exosome-dependent but polyadenylation-independent mechanism. Moreover, Trf4p but not Trf5p stimulates RNA degradation mechanisms that are functionally linked to telomere maintenance and to antisense RNA-mediated regulatory pathways of gene expression. These results suggest widespread and distinct roles of different TRAMP complexes in the regulation of gene expression.
###end p 11
###begin title 12
Results
###end title 12
###begin title 13
Trf4p and Trf5p Modulate the Expression of Different Sets of Genes
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 110 113 110 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Kadaba1">[4]</xref>
###xml 114 117 114 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 119 123 119 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Davis1">[14]</xref>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houalla1">[16]</xref>
###xml 266 279 266 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 301 305 301 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 307 316 307 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 321 325 317 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 327 336 323 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 589 610 581 602 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 843 852 835 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 860 869 848 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1057 1066 1041 1046 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1072 1081 1052 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1090 1109 1066 1081 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 1326 1330 1298 1302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Tusher1">[33]</xref>
###xml 1332 1341 1304 1313 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1390 1398 1362 1370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1468 1472 1440 1444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Baldi1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1520 1521 1492 1493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1546 1550 1518 1522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Baldi1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1581 1582 1553 1554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1594 1602 1566 1574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s008">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1747 1756 1719 1728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1833 1842 1805 1810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1847 1856 1815 1820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1993 2006 1957 1970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces</italic>
###xml 2029 2037 1993 2001 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s009">Table S3</xref>
###xml 266 279 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 377 382 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 452 457 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
TRAMP complexes promote the exosome-assisted degradation of diverse ncRNAs and aberrant or nonfunctional RNAs [4]-[7], [14]-[16]. To identify additional specific RNA targets for the TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 complexes, we measured the relative changes of gene expression of S. cerevisiae cells lacking either trf4 (trf4Delta) or trf5 (trf5Delta) compared to wild-type (WT) cells using yeast oligo microarrays that contained features representing all annotated yeast ORFs, ncRNAs, introns, rRNA precursors, as well as some intergenic regions (IGRs) and tiled regions downstream of a few genes (see Materials and Methods). To this purpose, total RNA isolated from exponentially growing cells was reverse transcribed with a mixture of random nonamers and oligo(dT) primers. Cy5 fluorescently labeled cDNAs derived from total RNA isolated from either the trf4Delta or the trf5Delta mutants were then competitively hybridized with Cy3 labeled cDNAs from WT cells. To define a list of arrayed features determining transcripts that significantly changed expression in the trf4Delta, the trf5Delta and the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutants (which are explained below), we arbitrarily selected those features that changed relative expression at least 2-fold (average of three biological replicates) with false discovery rates (FDRs) of less than 5% [33] (Figure 1A; a list of the selected features is provided in Table S1). Similar results were obtained by statistical analysis with Cyber-T [34] followed by selection of those features with a p-value of less than 0.05 [34] (for a comparison of FDRs and p-values see Table S2). To further visualize the relation among the 715 features selected by this analysis, we hierarchically clustered the features and experiments (Figure 1A). To identify common themes among the differentially expressed mRNAs in the trf4Delta and trf5Delta mutants, we searched for common Gene Ontology (GO) annotations among the 550 transcripts for which GO annotations were available at the Saccharomyces Genome Database (SGD; Table S3).
###end p 14

###xml 32 41 32 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 43 52 39 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 84 93 76 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 94 103 82 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
Features with altered levels in trf4Delta, trf5Delta, and polyadenylation-defective trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutants.
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 83 92 83 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 94 103 90 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 108 117 100 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 118 127 106 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 142 150 130 138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 246 255 234 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 259 268 243 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 330 349 310 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 351 355 327 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DADA</italic>
###xml 740 749 716 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 761 770 733 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 916 917 884 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
(A) Hierarchical cluster of 715 features that changed at least 2-fold (FDRs<5%) in trf4Delta, trf5Delta, or trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant cells (Table S1). Columns (1, 2, 3) correspond to individual experiments, rows to genes. The RNA levels in the trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutant strain relative to the WT (BY4741) strain, and in the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA (DADA) mutant strain relative to BY4741/pNOPPATA1L strain, are colored in the yellow-blue ratio scale as indicated at the bottom. Yellow shades indicate higher transcript abundance in mutants compared to WT, and blue shades represent lower transcript abundance. Grey represents missing values. Solid lines (I and II) mark the 422 and the 269 features that were selectively increased in the trf4Delta (I) or the trf5Delta (II) mutants, respectively. (B) Venn diagrams representing overlap of transcripts that were at least 2-fold increased in mutants compared to WT. P-values relate to the significance of the overlap (Fisher's Exact test, right tail).
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 92 95 92 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf</italic>
###xml 312 321 312 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 366 370 366 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 375 379 375 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 563 572 563 572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 626 635 626 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 644 653 640 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 719 728 711 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 804 808 796 800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SSB1</italic>
###xml 810 816 802 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HSP150</italic>
###xml 822 826 814 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TIR2</italic>
###xml 871 875 863 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TDH2</italic>
###xml 877 881 869 873 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TDH3</italic>
###xml 883 887 875 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADH2</italic>
###xml 893 897 885 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PDC1</italic>
###xml 927 931 919 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 936 940 928 932 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 998 1005 990 997 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1095 1099 1087 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1104 1108 1096 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1165 1172 1157 1164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Not surprisingly, most of the 715 selected features showed increased steady-state levels in trf mutants (691 features, 97%), which is in agreement with the idea that Trf4p and Trf5p promote RNA degradation and their depletion hence leads to the accumulation of RNAs that are normally targeted by these proteins (Figure 1A). More interestingly, although deletions of trf4 and trf5 are synthetically lethal, which may suggest common functions and targets, we found that the vast majority of the affected transcripts overlapped only marginally though significantly (Figure 1B). Only 33 transcripts changed expression in both the trf4Delta and the trf5Delta mutants; among these, 27 transcripts were selectively increased (Figure 1B) and represented rRNA processing intermediates, mRNAs encoding chaperones (SSB1, HSP150, and TIR2) or enzymes involved in glucose metabolism (TDH2, TDH3, ADH2, and PDC1). These results suggest that trf4 and trf5 specifically affect very different groups of transcripts in vivo. However, we wish to point out that the comparison of gene expression profiles of single trf4 and trf5 deletion mutants may not reveal the full spectra of the in vivo targets; particularly in cases where either functional Trf4 or Trf5 proteins can fully substitute the absence of the other paralog.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 33 36 33 36 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 38 41 38 41 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 43 47 43 47 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Davis1">[14]</xref>
###xml 48 52 48 52 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houalla1">[16]</xref>
###xml 123 132 123 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 302 312 298 308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1A</xref>
###xml 314 323 310 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 329 337 325 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 526 545 522 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 561 565 549 553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Neil1">[18]</xref>
###xml 595 604 583 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 647 651 631 635 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 732 740 716 724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
Consistent with previous reports [6], [7], [14]-[16], 72 of the 422 features (17%) that accumulated at least 2-fold in the trf4Delta mutant were ncRNAs, such as snoRNAs (27 features) and RNAs derived from intergenic regions (IGRs; 20 features), or autonomously replicating sequences (ARSs; 4 features; Figure S1A, Figure S2, and Table S1). Interestingly, 13 of the 20 IGRs overlap with CUTs that have been recently mapped by massive sequencing of RNAs bound to the nuclear cap-binding protein Cbp20p isolated from conditional trf4Delta rrp6Delta double mutants [18], or that were accumulated in rrp6Delta mutants and identified with tiling arrays [19]. (A comparison of selected IGRs and CUTs is provided in a separate worksheet of Table S1.)
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 110 119 110 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 128 137 124 133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 180 183 176 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyA</italic>
###xml 188 191 184 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyB</italic>
###xml 286 296 282 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 435 438 431 434 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyA</italic>
###xml 443 446 439 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyB</italic>
###xml 457 467 453 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s003">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 485 500 481 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; cells</italic>
###xml 567 576 559 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 667 676 643 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 679 689 651 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s003">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 748 753 720 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trans</italic>
###xml 825 828 797 800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyA</italic>
###xml 909 913 881 885 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Berretta1">[27]</xref>
###xml 951 955 923 927 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Berretta1">[27]</xref>
###xml 1025 1029 997 1001 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6</italic>
###xml 1109 1118 1081 1086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1171 1180 1127 1132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1189 1199 1141 1151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s003">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 1302 1311 1254 1259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1340 1349 1288 1293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1403 1412 1347 1352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 1507 1510 1447 1450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyA</italic>
###xml 1515 1518 1455 1458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyB</italic>
###xml 1597 1601 1537 1541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1605 1609 1545 1549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1776 1779 1716 1719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TY1</italic>
Ty1 retrotransposons represented the second most abundant class of transcripts with altered expression in the trf4Delta strain (Figure S1), as 68 out of the 98 probes specific for TyA and TyB exhibited an average 4-fold increase in relative expression levels compared to the WT strain (Figure S3A). This result was further confirmed by quantitative real-time PCR (qRT-PCR) analysis with primers specific for a sequence overlapping the TyA and TyB boundary (Figure S3B). In contrast to trf4Delta cells, the expression of the Ty1 elements was slightly decreased in the trf5Delta mutant (approximately-1.5-fold) and unchanged in cells lacking the exosome subunit Rrp6p (rrp6Delta) (Figure S3B). Ty1 transcription and transposition is regulated by the trans acting antisense regulatory RTL-RNA that is transcribed divergently to TyA from an internal promoter and is degraded by the 5' to 3' exoribonuclease Xrn1p [27]. In agreement with a previous report [27], we found that the steady state levels of RTL-RNA were unaffected in rrp6 mutants. Conversely, RTL-RNA levels were slightly increased (>1.5-fold) in the trf4Delta mutant and decreased (approximately1.5-fold) in the trf5Delta mutant (Figure S3B). Since both the Ty1 elements and the negative regulator RTL-RNA were simultaneously increased in the trf4Delta mutant and decreased in the trf5Delta mutant, but remained unchanged in the exosome mutant rrp6Delta, we speculate that the TRAMP/exosome pathway is not involved in either the degradation of the TyA and TyB mRNAs or of the antisense regulatory RTL-RNA. However, the opposite effect of trf4 or trf5 deletions on the levels of the TY1- and RTL-RNAs suggests that TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 likely act through a yet uncharacterized mechanism to regulate the expression of the TY1 locus.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 12 16 12 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 189 199 189 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1B</xref>
###xml 228 233 228 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SNR68</italic>
###xml 342 346 342 346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 348 356 348 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 394 398 394 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 623 624 623 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 698 699 698 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 739 740 739 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 784 785 784 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 842 850 842 850 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s009">Table S3</xref>
###xml 917 918 917 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 999 1008 999 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1073 1074 1069 1070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1077 1080 1073 1076 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;17</sup>
###xml 1126 1130 1122 1126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1134 1138 1130 1134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1293 1302 1289 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1307 1316 1299 1304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1325 1329 1313 1317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano1">[22]</xref>
###xml 1331 1335 1319 1323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Castano2">[24]</xref>
###xml 1336 1340 1324 1328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Edwards1">[26]</xref>
Deletion of TRF5 caused the accumulation of only 11 ncRNAs (4%) out of the 269 features (representing 220 GO annotated genes) for which we measured significantly altered expression levels (Figure S1B). This includes one snoRNA (SNR68), and four IGRs likely representing two CUTs (CUT857, CUT195) and the stable untranslated transcript SUT180 [19] (Table S1). However, the majority (94%) of the trf5-affected transcripts can be assigned to protein-coding mRNAs. A GO analysis among these messages revealed overrepresentation of mRNAs coding for cytoplasmic proteins involved in translation (e.g. 19 ribosomal protein genes, p<0.01) or act in diverse metabolic processes such as glycolysis (7 genes, p<0.01), sulphate assimilation (5 genes, p<0.003), and nitrogen metabolism (21 genes, p<0.003; GO analysis of annotated transcripts is shown in Table S3). Except for 7 messages coding for proteins acting in glycolysis (p<0.01), these themes could not be seen among the mRNAs that were affected in the trf4Delta mutant which preferentially encode nuclear proteins (116 genes, p<10-17). In conclusion, it appears that deletion of trf4 or trf5 affected the steady-state level of a large variety of mRNAs that function in diverse cellular pathways and may reflect in part the pleiotropic defects of trf4Delta and trf5Delta mutants [22], [24]-[26]. Our results also indicate that degradation of ncRNAs is mainly promoted by Trf4p.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 65 89 65 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 65 89 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
TRF4-Mediated Polyadenylation Is Dispensable for Most Targets in Saccharomyces cerevisiae
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 163 182 163 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 241 250 237 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 250 253 246 249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 281 290 277 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 322 326 314 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NOP1</italic>
###xml 341 362 333 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 495 498 487 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 547 556 539 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 565 574 553 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 621 640 605 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
We next aimed at identifying the set of transcripts that require the polyadenylation activity of Trf4 for efficient degradation. For this purpose we constructed a trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant strain, where the polyadenylation defective allele TRF4-DADA[5] is episomally expressed in trf4Delta cells under the control of the NOP1 promoter (see Materials and Methods). Trf4p-DADA contains two aspartate to alanine mutations in the poly(A) polymerase catalytic site which renders the enzyme inactive [5]. Similar to the microarray experiments with the trf4Delta and the trf5Delta mutants, we compared transcript levels of the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant to that of the WT strain harboring the empty vector (BY4741/pNOPPATA1L).
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 103 112 103 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 195 204 191 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 213 221 209 217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 223 233 219 229 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1C</xref>
###xml 320 329 316 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 356 365 352 361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 397 407 393 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1C</xref>
###xml 517 536 513 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 553 562 545 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 577 585 565 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 763 772 751 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 774 782 762 770 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 834 838 822 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NME1</italic>
###xml 891 900 879 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YJL047C-A</italic>
###xml 902 911 890 899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YBR072C-A</italic>
###xml 913 922 901 910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YGR121W-A</italic>
###xml 928 937 916 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YBR182C-A</italic>
###xml 966 975 954 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 984 988 968 972 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 1399 1406 1383 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Surprisingly, the expression levels of more than 90% of transcripts that were significantly altered in trf4Delta mutant cells were almost fully restored to WT levels by the overexpression of the TRF4-DADA allele (Figure 1, Figure S1C). Only 57 transcripts were more than 2-fold enriched (FDR<5%) in cells expressing the TRF4-DADA allele as compared to WT (Figure 1B), 18 of them (32%) are ncRNAs (Figure S1C). Although the relative abundance of most SGD annotated rRNA intermediates, snoRNAs, and IGRs was reduced in trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA compared to the trf4Delta mutant cells (Table S1), 31 ncRNAs (7 rRNA intermediates, 15 SNRs, and 9 IGRs) still exhibited increased steady-state levels (on average between 1.5-fold and 4-fold; FDR<5%) relative to the WT cells (Figure S2, Table S1). Similar results were found for the RNA component NME1 of RNase MRP and for a group of short dubious ORFs (YJL047C-A, YBR072C-A, YGR121W-A, and YBR182C-A) that were also enriched in rrp6Delta mutants [19] and, hence, most likely do not encode proteins but rather correspond to CUTs. Some of these ncRNAs are highly abundant such as rRNAs and snoRNAs. It therefore appears that highly expressed and structured RNAs strongly depend on the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p although they represent only a minor fraction (10%) of Trf4 targets. However, this fraction may recruit a considerable amount of Trf4 complexes in vivo and thus, a substantial fraction of the total RNA turnover mediated by Trf4p may depend upon Trf4 catalytic activity.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Trf4p Stimulates the Degradation of a Subgroup of Introns
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 231 240 231 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 280 289 276 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 322 331 314 323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 333 341 325 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 654 670 646 662 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2B and 2C</xref>
###xml 786 795 778 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 931 940 919 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 945 964 929 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 974 983 954 963 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 985 993 965 973 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1078 1083 1058 1063 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 1085 1090 1065 1070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 1096 1100 1076 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GCR1</italic>
###xml 1139 1148 1119 1124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1295 1300 1271 1276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 1302 1307 1278 1283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 1313 1317 1289 1293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GCR1</italic>
###xml 1443 1452 1419 1424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1482 1491 1454 1463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
In addition to ncRNAs such as rRNA intermediates, snoRNAs, and IGR RNAs/CUTs, our microarray data showed that a group of introns, some of which containing snoRNAs, were specifically accumulated (2- to 8-fold; FDR<5%) in either the trf4Delta mutant (Trf4-dependent introns) or the trf5Delta mutant (Trf5-dependent introns; Figure 2A, Table S1). To rule out that accumulation of these introns simply reflects increased transcript levels of the pre-mRNAs, we compared the relative changes of intron abundance with that of the corresponding pre-mRNAs and mature mRNAs as revealed with arrayed probes that specifically detect intron-exon junctions and exons (Figure 2B and 2C). We found that unlike introns, the corresponding pre-mRNAs and mature mRNAs were not significantly changed in the trf4Delta mutant compared to WT cells. Likewise, the cognate pre-mRNAs and mature mRNAs of the Trf4-dependent introns were also unchanged in the trf5Delta and trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutants (Figure 2B, Table S1). Thus, this analysis indicates that only spliced-out introns, such as those of the RPS9A, RPL7B, and GCR1 genes, specifically accumulate in the trf4Delta mutant. To validate this finding, we carried out qRT-PCR experiments with primers either specific for the introns, the pre-mRNAs, or the mRNAs of RPS9A, RPL7B, and GCR1. Consistent with our microarray data, the levels of introns but not those of pre-mRNAs or mature mRNAs were increased in the trf4Delta mutant compared to WT cells (Figure S4 and results not shown).
###end p 25
###begin title 26
Trf4p promotes polyadenylation-independent degradation of introns.
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 78 87 78 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 91 100 87 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 142 151 134 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 269 277 257 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 307 310 295 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">snR</italic>
###xml 369 374 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 392 397 380 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 619 624 607 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 706 711 694 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 766 767 754 755 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 808 818 796 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s013">Dataset S1</xref>
###xml 899 905 887 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL16A</italic>
###xml 923 929 911 917 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL40A</italic>
###xml 1127 1134 1115 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1164 1183 1152 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1217 1221 1197 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1225 1229 1205 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 1264 1269 1244 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pGAL1</italic>
###xml 1341 1345 1321 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1351 1355 1331 1335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 1430 1434 1404 1408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1440 1444 1414 1418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 1486 1491 1460 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 1496 1502 1470 1476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL40A</italic>
###xml 1530 1535 1504 1509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 1663 1664 1637 1638 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1703 1704 1677 1678 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 1702 1704 1676 1678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t<sub>0</sub></italic>
###xml 1818 1839 1792 1813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
(A) Microarray data for 18 introns that changed more than 2-fold (FDRs<5%) in trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutants. Overexpression of Trf4p-DADA in trf4Delta mutant cells reduced steady-state levels of most of these introns to WT levels. Microarrays are the same as shown in Figure 1. Introns containing snoRNAs (snR) are indicated. (B) Relative changes of the expression of RPL7B (left panel) and RPS9A (right panel) introns, pre-mRNAs, and mature mRNAs as revealed by exon (ex), intron (int), and intron-exon junction probes (pre) present on the microarrays. Int-1 and int-2 refer to the first and the second intron of the RPL7B gene; pre-1 and pre-2 refer to the respective intron-exon junction probes of the RPL7B pre-mRNA. The height of the bar represents average log2 ratios from triplicate microarray data (Dataset S1); error bars show the standard deviation. (C) Relative changes of expression of RPL16A (left panel) and RPL40A (right panel) introns (int), pre-mRNAs (pre) and mature mRNAs (ex). Data was extracted from triplicate microarray data as described above. (D) Depletion of Trf4p or Trf5p promotes intron stability in vivo. Total RNA was purified from trf4Delta trf5Delta mutant strains either expressing TRF4 or TRF5, which were transcribed under the pGAL1 promoter. Cells were initially grown in a galactose containing medium (TRF4 Gal; TRF5 Gal) and then shifted to a glucose containing medium (YPD) at 30degreesC (TRF4 Glc; TRF5 Glc) for 1 h. Accumulation of introns of RPS9A and RPL40A and of the first intron of RPL7B was determined by qRT-PCR with intron-specific primers. The steady-state levels of introns in each sample was calculated as log2 of normalized ratios relative to the t0 time point, which corresponds to the cultures immediately before the galactose to glucose shift (for details see Materials and Methods). The values represent averages from two independent qRT-PCR analyses.
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 105 108 105 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 114 117 114 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 178 187 178 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 210 229 206 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 287 296 279 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 342 346 330 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6</italic>
###xml 428 433 416 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 435 440 423 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 446 450 434 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GCR1</italic>
###xml 465 474 453 462 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 530 539 518 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 550 559 538 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 706 715 690 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 717 726 701 710 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 728 736 712 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 909 916 893 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
As Trf4p promotes the exosome-mediated degradation of targeted RNAs through its polyadenylation activity [1], [5]-[7], we also analyzed the steady-state levels of introns in the rrp6Delta exosome mutant and in trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant cells. Similarly to what has been observed in the trf4Delta mutant, introns accumulated in cells lacking rrp6 but no significant change in the expression of the pre-mRNAs and mature mRNAs of RPS9A, RPL7B, and GCR1 was detected (Figure S4 and data not shown). Conversely, overexpression of the TRF4-DADA allele in trf4Delta cells restored WT levels for nine of the 13 Trf4-dependent introns, or reduced their abundance to values slightly above (1.5 fold) the WT levels (Figure 2A, Figure S4, Table S1, and results not shown). This indicates that the polyadenylation-defective Trf4-DADA protein also participates in the regulation of "normal" steady-state levels of introns in vivo.
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 34 43 34 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 113 122 109 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 124 134 120 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL16A-INT</italic>
###xml 139 149 135 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL40A-INT</italic>
###xml 153 162 149 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 249 258 245 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 260 268 256 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 347 356 343 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
Unlike to what we observed in the trf4Delta mutant, however, the increased levels of the Trf5-dependent introns (Figure 2A; RPL16A-INT and RPL40A-INT in Figure S4) coincided with similar amounts of the related pre-mRNAs and mature mRNA transcripts (Figure 2C, Table S1, and data not shown), strongly suggesting that accumulation of introns in the trf5Delta mutant reflects increased relative abundance of unspliced pre-mRNAs.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 164 168 164 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 238 257 238 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 325 329 317 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 333 337 325 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 363 367 355 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL1</italic>
###xml 394 415 386 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 430 439 422 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 528 532 520 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 536 540 528 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
To test whether Trf5p could efficiently target spliced-out introns in the absence of Trf4p, we analyzed intron accumulation by qRT-PCR experiments upon conditional TRF4 or TRF5 depletion. In this experiment, total RNA was isolated from a trf4Delta trf5Delta double mutant strain complemented with a plasmid either expressing TRF4 or TRF5 under the control of the GAL1 promoter (for details see Materials and Methods). As shown in Figure 2D, an one hour shift of cells to media supplemented with glucose to repress expression of TRF4 or TRF5, led to an enrichment of all the introns tested. Conversely, no change in the abundance of introns was observed in control experiments performed with total RNA purified from WT cells that were transformed with the empty vector (BY4741/pYC6-CT; results not shown).
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 223 227 223 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF5</italic>
###xml 231 240 231 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 274 281 270 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 358 367 354 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
Taken together, these results suggest that Trf4p likely promotes the exosome-mediated degradation of a group of spliced-out introns through a mechanism that is not dependent on polyadenylation. In addition, as depletion of TRF5 in trf4Delta cells caused intron accumulation in vivo, we infer that Trf4p and Trf5p are functionally redundant for intron decay (Figure 2D).
###end p 31
###begin title 32
###xml 30 37 30 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In Vivo</italic>
TRAMP4 Interacts with Introns In Vivo
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 54 61 54 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 421 442 421 442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 578 581 578 581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 904 913 904 913 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 990 993 990 993 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 994 997 994 997 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 1111 1120 1111 1120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
To identify RNAs associated with TRAMP4, we performed in vivo cross-linking and ribonucleoprotein-immunopurification experiments followed by microarray analysis of bound RNAs (X-RIP-Chip). Cells expressing recombinant tandem-affinity purification (TAP)-tagged Trf4 protein were cross-linked with formaldehyde, and Trf4-containing ribonucleoprotein complexes were recovered by affinity selection on IgG-coupled beads (see Materials and Methods). Cells expressing TAP-tagged Trf4 proteins fully restore Trf4 functions and were previously used to purify functional TRAMP complexes [5]. As a control for non-specifically enriched RNAs, the same experiment was done with untagged WT cells and with cells expressing Fpr1-TAP, a peptidyl-prolyl-cis-trans-isomerase not expected to bind RNA. About 70% of Trf4-TAP and 60% of Fpr1-TAP was captured from the whole cell extract (WCE) as shown by dot-blot analysis (Figure 3A, left panel). Moreover, Air2p, a well-known component of the TRAMP4 complex [5],[6], co-purified with crosslinked Trf4-TAP but was absent in control purifications performed with untagged WT cells (Figure 3A, right panel).
###end p 33
###begin title 34
Selective enrichment of introns in TRAMP4 affinity-isolates.
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 109 116 109 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1368 1369 1360 1361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1574 1583 1566 1571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1585 1604 1573 1588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 1606 1615 1590 1595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1621 1630 1601 1606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
