###xml 1662 1671 1638 1643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbr1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1735 1740 1701 1706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SC311</italic>
###xml 1745 1762 1711 1724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4(ts)trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1762 1766 1724 1728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wang1">[25]</xref>
(A) RNA-protein complexes were purified from extracts of cells expressing recombinant Trf4-TAP protein after in vivo cross-linking with formaldehyde (Trf4-TAP-X). Extracts of BY4741 cells and of cells expressing Fpr1-TAP were used as control (BY4741-X; Fpr1-TAP-X). Affinity purification of the Trf4-TAP protein complex or Fpr1-TAP from the WCEs was monitored by dot blot (left panel) and immunoblot (right panel) analyses with antibodies detecting the calmodulin-binding region of the TAP-tag (alpha-TAP) or the Air2p subunit of the TRAMP4 complex (alpha-Air2). Input and supernatant correspond to cross-linked WCEs before and after immunopurification, respectively. Affinity purified TAP-tagged Trf4 protein complex from non cross-linked WCEs was used as a positive control for the purification procedure (Trf4-TAP). A molecular weight marker is shown next to the immunoblot; * denotes likely Air2p degradation products. (B, C) Percentile rank analysis of immunopurified RNA preparations. RNAs enriched by TAP-tag affinity purification was comparatively analyzed to total RNA purified from WCEs with DNA microarrays. The enrichment profiles of introns (B) and the respective ORFs (C) were created by binning average percentile ranks from three biological replicates of Trf4-TAP or control IPs (two replicates of Fpr1-TAP and one untagged cells) into 0.05 unit bins. P-values to estimate the difference between Trf4 and control data were calculated with the Kolmogorov-Smirnov test. (D) Northern analysis with intron- and exon- specific probes in RNA surveillance mutants (trf4Delta, trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta) and in the debranching enzyme dbr1Delta mutant strain. Strains were grown at 30degreesC in YPD, except SC311 and trf4(ts)trf5Delta[25] that were shifted to 37degreesC for the indicated times prior to RNA extraction.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 428 432 428 432 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Gerber1">[35]</xref>
###xml 433 437 433 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Gerber2">[36]</xref>
###xml 646 656 646 656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s014">Dataset S2</xref>
###xml 247 252 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We isolated total RNA from extracts (input) and from the immunopurified samples and labeled cDNAs derived from the RNAs with Cy3 and Cy5 fluorescent dyes, respectively. The differentially labeled samples were mixed and competitively hybridized on yeast oligo arrays. In this assay, the ratio of the two RNA populations at a given array element provides a measurement for enrichment of the respective RNA with the TRAMP4 complex [35],[36]. Because of the relatively high variation of array data between biological replicates, we rank ordered the data and determined percentile ranks for each analyzed feature (0, no enrichment; 1 high enrichment; Dataset S2).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 566 567 566 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 576 578 576 578 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 580 589 580 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 631 639 631 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s010">Table S4</xref>
###xml 707 708 707 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 717 726 717 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 978 987 978 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 996 1004 992 1000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1009 1018 1005 1014 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 1094 1103 1090 1095 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1108 1117 1100 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1127 1136 1115 1124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 1252 1260 1240 1248 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s010">Table S4</xref>
In agreement with known functions of TRAMP4 on ncRNAs, we found that many small and stable ncRNAs such as snoRNAs and tRNAs were highly enriched in purified cross-linked TRAMP4 complexes. However, these transcripts were also strongly enriched in the control isolates and thus, only limited conclusions can be drawn from this analysis. Nevertheless, despite the high background from small ncRNAs in these experiments, we found that spliced-out introns were selectively enriched in the Trf4-TAP RNA isolates when compared to control isolates (Kolmogorov-Smirnov test: p = 2.5x10-5; Figure 3B, data for all intron probes are shown in Table S4). The corresponding probes for the mature mRNAs were not enriched (p = 0.12; Figure 3C), suggesting specific association of the TRAMP4 complex with spliced introns but not with the respective pre-mRNAs. This finding is consistent with our previous observation for accumulation of certain introns but not of the corresponding mRNAs in the trf4Delta mutant (Figure 2 and Figure S4): For 11 (78%) of the 14 introns that were significantly changed in either trf4Delta and trf5Delta mutants (Figure 2A) and for which X-RIP-Chip data were available, we found higher ranking with TRAMP4 complexes compared to controls (Table S4), whereas no such preference was seen for the respective ORF probes (two of the six corresponding ORFs were higher ranked with TRAMP4 complexes).
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 111 120 111 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 124 133 120 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 340 349 332 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 353 362 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 383 384 367 368 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 412 421 396 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 426 435 406 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 451 459 427 435 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s010">Table S4</xref>
###xml 721 727 697 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS24A</italic>
###xml 732 737 708 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL2B</italic>
###xml 916 920 892 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 925 929 901 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1067 1076 1043 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 1138 1142 1110 1114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbr1</italic>
###xml 1207 1211 1175 1179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Chapman1">[37]</xref>
###xml 1212 1216 1180 1184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Khalid1">[39]</xref>
###xml 1218 1227 1186 1195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3D</xref>
###xml 1319 1328 1287 1292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1336 1345 1300 1305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1445 1462 1405 1418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4(ts)trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1529 1534 1485 1490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS9A</italic>
###xml 1536 1541 1492 1497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL7B</italic>
###xml 1547 1553 1503 1509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL40A</italic>
###xml 1627 1636 1583 1592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 1758 1765 1714 1721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
We further analyzed whether expression levels of the TRAMP4 associated introns were commonly changed in single trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutants. The relative expression levels for 48 introns that were preferentially enriched with TRAMP4 complexes (percentile ranks greater than 0.85) compared to the controls, were mostly unchanged in either trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutants (average log2 ratios = 0.035 and -0.1 in trf4Delta and trf5Delta, respectively; Table S4). Possibly, Trf4p and Trf5p act redundantly in the decay of most spliced-out introns and therefore no changes of relative expression levels can be seen in single mutants. To further corroborate this idea, we measured the expression of introns for the two genes RPS24A and RPL2B that were enriched in TRAMP4 affinity isolates (average percentile ranks of 0.83 and 0.9, respectively) but for which expression levels were not significantly changed in neither trf4 nor trf5 mutants, by Northern blot analysis with intron specific probes. As expected, these introns were detectable in total RNA derived from the rrp6Delta exosome mutant and from the mutant of the debranching enzyme dbr1Delta, which was used as a positive control for intron detection [37]-[39] (Figure 3D). However, both introns could not be readily detected in total RNA derived from either the trf4Delta or the trf5Delta single mutant strains, but they were strongly accumulated in RNA samples isolated from conditional trf4(ts)trf5Delta double mutants. This result is reminiscent of our finding for the RPS9A, RPL7B, and RPL40A introns that became increasingly enriched in conditional double mutants (Figure 2D). In conclusion, these data strongly suggest functional redundancy between Trf4p and Trf5p in the degradation of introns in vivo.
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 4 13 4 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
The trf4Delta Mutant Is Defective in the Turnover of Subtelomeric RNAs
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 315 324 315 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 326 330 326 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Yamada1">[40]</xref>
###xml 446 452 446 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL05L</italic>
###xml 532 536 532 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 602 611 602 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML&#945;1</italic>
###xml 616 626 612 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS318-HMR</italic>
###xml 699 706 695 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YBL109W</italic>
###xml 708 715 704 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YDR543C</italic>
###xml 717 724 713 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YHR217C</italic>
###xml 730 737 726 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKL225W</italic>
###xml 767 776 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 785 794 777 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 804 812 792 800 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 814 823 802 811 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 829 839 817 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s005">Figure S5A</xref>
###xml 932 938 920 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL02L</italic>
###xml 940 946 928 934 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL04R</italic>
###xml 952 958 940 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL08R</italic>
###xml 969 975 957 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL11L</italic>
###xml 1002 1011 990 999 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 1059 1063 1047 1051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 1272 1276 1260 1264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Luke1">[41]</xref>
###xml 1339 1348 1327 1336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 1401 1410 1389 1394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1506 1515 1490 1499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 1582 1601 1566 1581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 1713 1720 1693 1700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1722 1731 1702 1711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 1778 1785 1758 1765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YDR543C</italic>
###xml 1790 1797 1770 1777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKL225W</italic>
###xml 1838 1842 1818 1822 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1876 1885 1856 1865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 1921 1930 1901 1906 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1944 1953 1920 1925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 2039 2043 2011 2015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR2</italic>
###xml 2045 2049 2017 2021 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR3</italic>
###xml 2055 2060 2027 2032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MCM10</italic>
###xml 2077 2081 2049 2053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS5</italic>
###xml 2113 2123 2085 2095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s005">Figure S5B</xref>
###xml 2190 2199 2162 2167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Yeast telomeres (TEL) consist of a complex mosaic of telomeric and subtelomeric sequences, where the X element sequence is the only region common to all chromosome ends. Some subtelomeric regions contain a conserved helicase-encoding repetitive sequence (Y' sequence) located within terminal telomeric repeats (TR; Figure 4A) [40]. It has recently been reported that cryptic transcripts originating from transcriptionally repressed loci, such as TEL05L, accumulate in strains lacking components of the TRAMP4 or the exosome complex [30]. Consistent with this, we found that transcripts spanning across HMLalpha1 and ARS318-HMR of the silenced mating cassettes and across putative subtelomeric ORFs (YBL109W, YDR543C, YHR217C, and YKL225W) were highly abundant in the trf4Delta and the rrp6Delta mutants (Table S1, Figure 4B, and Figure S5A). In particular, the subtelomeric transcripts originate from telomeres that either contain (TEL02L, TEL04R, and TEL08R) or lack (TEL11L) the Y' sequence element (Figure 4B). Similar to what has been reported previously [30], they are commonly oriented in the 5' to 3' direction towards the centromere (results not shown). Neither subtelomeric RNAs transcribed from the opposite strand towards the telomeres nor telomeric TERRA RNAs [41] were detected (results not shown). Although overexpression of TRF4-DADA reduced the abundance of these subtelomeric RNAs in trf4Delta mutant cells, their steady-state levels were still about 1.5-2.2 fold higher than in WT cells (Figure 4B). This decrease in the abundance of subtelomeric RNAs seen in the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant indicates that the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p may enhance the degradation of these RNA molecules in vivo (Figure 4B). Increased expression for two of these RNAs (YDR543C and YKL225W) was also found in strains deficient of trf5 as shown by qRT-PCR experiments (Figure 4B). Interestingly and in contrast to trf4Delta mutants, the trf5Delta mutant exhibited also changes in the relative expression of factors that positively (SIR2, SIR3, and MCM10) or negatively (SAS5) regulate chromatin silencing (Figure S5B). Thus, it could be that accumulation of subtelomeric RNAs in the trf5Delta mutant reflects defects in pathways other than RNA turnover.
###end p 40
###begin title 41
Subtelomeric transcripts are detected in strains defective in RNA surveillance pathways.
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 345 348 345 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 613 617 613 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACT1</italic>
###xml 722 723 722 723 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 866 875 866 875 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 32 37 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
(A) Schematic representation of yeast telomeres. X-type telomeres consist of the X element core sequences (XC), the subtelomeric repeats (STR), and the telomeric repeats at the ends of the chromosomes. The Y'-type telomeres contain a subtelomeric Y' DNA sequence located within the telomeric repeats that is not found in X telomers. A conserved XhoI restriction site specific for Y' sequences is shown. (B) Bar diagram representing the qRT-PCR analysis for four subtelomeric ORFs transcribed from X- and Y'-type telomeric regions. Corresponding telomeres are indicated in brackets. RNA amounts were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and are compared relative to the isogenic WT strain. Relative changes of transcript abundances (log2 ratio scale) represent averages from two independent qRT-PCR analyses. The same RNA preparation was used for the microarray analysis shown in Figure 1A.
###end p 42
###begin title 43
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 65 74 65 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
Telomere Shortening Correlates with Increased TLC1 Expression in trf4Delta Mutants
###end title 43
###begin p 44
###xml 165 168 165 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 243 259 243 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5A and 5B</xref>
###xml 331 340 319 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 378 387 350 355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 404 413 372 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 499 508 467 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 522 531 486 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 612 616 572 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 618 627 578 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 675 684 635 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 742 751 698 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 817 826 773 782 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 878 887 834 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
To test whether any correlation existed between subtelomeric RNA accumulation and the structural integrity of telomeres, we performed Southern blot experiments with XhoI digested genomic DNA to determine the length of Y' containing telomeres (Figure 5A and 5B). Y' telomeres were on average shortened by approximately120 bp in the trf4Delta mutant and approximately40 bp in the rrp6Delta exosome mutant (Figure 5A). Conversely, the length of Y' telomeres was similar to that of the WT strain in the trf5Delta mutant or in trf4Delta mutant cells complemented with a plasmid (pNOPPATA1L) carrying the WT allele of TRF4 (Figure 5A). Intriguingly, shortening of telomeres in the trf4Delta mutant was also strongly suppressed by overexpression of TRF4-DADA, where telomeres were about 40 bp shorter than in the WT strain (Figure 5B). These results showed that telomere shortening in trf4Delta cells is a reversible event achieved by reintroduction of episomally expressed Trf4 proteins. In addition, our results strongly suggest that Trf4p exerts a role in telomere maintenance mainly through a mechanism that is independent of polyadenylation.
###end p 44
###begin title 45
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
Trf4p promotes telomere maintenance and TLC1 regulation through a polyadenylation-independent mechanism.
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 72 75 72 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 119 128 119 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 130 149 126 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 151 160 143 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 166 175 154 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 180 193 164 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 315 324 299 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 347 356 327 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 400 404 376 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DADA</italic>
###xml 412 416 388 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DADA</italic>
###xml 459 478 435 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 590 593 562 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 778 787 750 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 792 801 760 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 802 811 766 775 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 909 913 873 877 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 949 958 913 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 960 979 920 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 981 990 937 942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 996 1005 948 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 1039 1043 987 991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACT1</italic>
###xml 1135 1136 1083 1084 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1271 1280 1219 1228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 180 193 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
(A, B) Southern blot analyses of Y'-type telomeres was carried out with XhoI-digested DNA of RNA surveillance mutants (trf4Delta, trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta) of S. cerevisiae probed with telomeric sequences. Mutant strains are indicated at the top: wt corresponds to the wild-type BY4741 strain; trf4Delta/vector represents the trf4Delta mutant strain transformed with pNOPPATA1L. DADA(1) and DADA (2) represent two different clones of the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant. A marker (M) for DNA sizes in kilobases is shown to the left. Solid black bars flanked by Y' shows the XhoI-digested Y' DNA fragments, where white bars refer to the position of average size fragments. Numbers in brackets refer to the average shortening of the Y'-containing telomeres in the trf4Delta and trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutants relative to wt. (C) qRT-PCR analysis examining the levels of specified mRNAs and ncRNAs (TLC1) in four RNA surveillance mutants (trf4Delta, trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta). RNA amounts were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and compared to the isogenic WT strain. Relative changes of transcript abundances (log2 ratio scale) represent averages from two independent qRT-PCR analyses. The same RNA was used for the microarray analysis presented in Figure 1A.
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 236 245 236 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 269 278 265 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 286 305 278 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 321 330 309 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 352 356 340 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 441 448 429 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YDR543C</italic>
###xml 453 460 441 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKL225W</italic>
###xml 462 471 450 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 504 513 492 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 585 594 569 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
The results from these Southern blotting experiments do not indicate any straight correlation between telomere shortening and accumulation of the subtelomeric RNA molecules. In fact, although subtelomeric RNAs were more abundant in the rrp6Delta mutant compared to the trf4Delta or the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant strain (Figure 4B), only disruption of trf4 resulted in a severe shortening of the telomeres. Moreover, some subtelomeric RNAs (YDR543C and YKL225W; Figure 4B) also highly accumulated in the trf5Delta mutant, which did not show any recognizable change in telomere length (Figure 5A).
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 178 182 178 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 184 188 184 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST1</italic>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST2</italic>
###xml 200 204 200 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST3</italic>
###xml 215 224 215 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Peterson1">[42]</xref>
###xml 231 235 231 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Smogorzewska1">[43]</xref>
###xml 244 253 244 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 499 503 495 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 538 547 534 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 591 595 583 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST1</italic>
###xml 597 601 589 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST2</italic>
###xml 607 611 599 603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST3</italic>
###xml 626 635 618 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 677 681 669 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 835 839 827 831 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Peterson1">[42]</xref>
###xml 893 897 885 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1007 1016 999 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1108 1117 1096 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 1173 1182 1161 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1252 1256 1236 1240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1283 1292 1267 1276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 1351 1355 1335 1339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1462 1466 1446 1450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1529 1533 1513 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1555 1564 1539 1544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1573 1582 1553 1562 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 1660 1669 1640 1645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1753 1757 1729 1733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST3</italic>
###xml 1759 1763 1735 1739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CST6</italic>
###xml 1769 1774 1745 1750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MET18</italic>
###xml 1826 1833 1802 1809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1835 1844 1811 1820 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 1846 1850 1822 1826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Askree1">[44]</xref>
###xml 712 717 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
To investigate whether misregulation of the telomerase components could be the cause of the telomere shortening, we carried out qRT-PCR experiments with primers specific for the TLC1, EST1, EST2, and EST3 subunits (Figure 5C) [42],[43]. In the rrp6Delta mutant, the steady-state levels for the mRNAs encoding these telomerase subunits were more than 2-fold increased compared to the WT strain, suggesting a consequent increase in the activity of the holoenzyme in this mutant. In contrast, only the TLC1 RNA was 2.6-fold increased in the trf4Delta mutant, whereas no change was detected for EST1, EST2, and EST3 mRNAs levels (Figure 5C). It was reported that overexpression of TLC1 causes telomere shortening in yeast because of the specific sequestration of the telomeric factors yKu70 and yKu80, which promote telomerase recruitment [42]. Thus, the imbalance in the expression level between TLC1 and the other subunits of the telomerase may in part account for for the telomere shortening observed in the trf4Delta mutant. This hypothesis is further supported by the observation that overexpression of the TRF4-DADA allele not only suppressed the telomeric defect of the trf4Delta mutant, but also coincided with the restoration of expression of the TLC1 RNA subunit to WT levels (Figure 5C). Furthermore, these results indicate that Trf4p promotes TLC1 turnover through a polyadenylation-independent mechanism. Consistent with the proposed connection between TLC1 overexpression and telomere shortening, we found no change of TLC1 RNA abundance in the trf5Delta mutant (Figure 5C). It is noteworthy, however, that the unaltered telomere length found in the trf5Delta mutant might also reflect increased expression levels (>3-fold) of factors such as EST3, CST6, and MET18, which participate in the maintenance of telomeres in vivo (Figure 5C) [44].
###end p 48
###begin title 49
Trf4p and the Exosome Promote Degradation of Antisense RNAs
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO3</italic>
###xml 232 236 232 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 238 243 238 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO11</italic>
###xml 245 250 245 250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO12</italic>
###xml 256 261 256 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO89</italic>
###xml 293 301 293 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 410 419 410 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 475 483 475 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 485 494 485 494 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 500 508 500 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
Besides the many mRNAs for which relative expression levels were significantly increased in strains devoid of Trf4p or Trf5p, the expression of a few genes including those coding for proteins involved in phosphate metabolism (PHO3, PHO5, PHO11, PHO12, and PHO89) were significantly decreased (Table S1). The relative abundance of these mRNAs was almost fully restored to WT levels by the overexpression of the TRF4-DADA allele as shown by microarray and qRT-PCR experiments (Figure 6, Figure S6, and Table S1).
###end p 50

Trf4p participates in antisense RNA-mediated regulation of genes of the phosphate metabolism.
