###begin p 53
###xml 31 34 31 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
###xml 102 106 102 106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houalla1">[16]</xref>
###xml 125 130 125 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO84</italic>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 288 292 288 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 293 297 293 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Camblong1">[29]</xref>
###xml 298 302 298 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Uhler1">[45]</xref>
Such reduced expression of the PHO genes has also previously been observed in nuclear exosome mutants [16]. Particularly for PHO84 and PHO5, it was shown that Rrp6p affects the stability of corresponding antisense RNAs involved in the transcriptional control of their cognate sense mRNAs [19],[29],[45].
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 48 53 48 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO11</italic>
###xml 59 64 59 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO89</italic>
###xml 74 83 74 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 85 94 81 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 100 109 92 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 305 308 293 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
###xml 327 336 315 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 338 347 326 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 492 501 480 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 506 515 490 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 527 536 507 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 630 639 606 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 641 650 617 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 661 665 637 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 670 675 646 651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO89</italic>
###xml 689 698 665 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s006">Figure S6</xref>
###xml 723 728 699 704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO84</italic>
###xml 728 732 704 708 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Camblong1">[29]</xref>
###xml 752 756 728 732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 758 763 734 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO11</italic>
###xml 769 774 745 750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO89</italic>
###xml 1034 1037 1010 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
###xml 1099 1103 1075 1079 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO5</italic>
###xml 1105 1110 1081 1086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO11</italic>
###xml 1116 1121 1092 1097 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO89</italic>
###xml 1268 1271 1244 1247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
To assess whether the decreased levels of PHO5, PHO11, and PHO89 mRNAs in trf4Delta, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta exosome mutants correlates with increased levels of corresponding antisense RNAs, we carried out strand-specific qRT-PCR experiments with primers specific for antisense RNAs that span across the PHO promoter regions (Figure 6B, Figure S6). Antisense RNAs could be detected in all the strains tested, including the WT strain, however, their levels were more than 2-fold increased in trf4Delta and rrp6Delta but not in trf5Delta mutants. The abundance of the antisense RNAs was decreased to WT levels by overexpression of TRF4-DADA (Figure 6B, data for PHO5 and PHO89 are shown in Figure S6). Therefore, similar to PHO84[29], the expression of PHO5, PHO11, and PHO89 is likely modulated by antisense RNAs, the degradation of which is promoted by the exosome and the Trf4 protein, and does not require the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p. In addition, although loss of Trf5p did not cause any change in the expression of the PHO antisense transcripts, the reduced steady state level of the PHO5, PHO11, and PHO89 mRNAs suggests that Trf5p, through an yet unknown mechanism, may also participate with Trf4p and the exosome in fine tuning the expression of the PHO genes.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Discussion
###end title 55
###begin title 56
Identification of RNAs Regulated by Trf4p and Trf5p
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 202 205 202 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 207 210 207 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Kadaba1">[4]</xref>
###xml 211 214 211 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Egecioglu1">[15]</xref>
###xml 220 224 220 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trf4</italic>
###xml 235 239 235 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 333 342 333 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 421 428 417 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 428 431 424 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 432 435 428 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 436 440 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 630 643 626 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 705 713 701 709 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 715 723 711 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 854 863 850 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 871 880 863 868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1062 1065 1050 1053 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 1067 1070 1055 1058 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 1071 1074 1059 1062 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1075 1079 1063 1067 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 1174 1178 1162 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1183 1187 1171 1175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 1246 1255 1234 1243 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1479 1483 1467 1471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houalla1">[16]</xref>
###xml 630 643 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Trf4p and Trf5p are non-canonical poly(A) polymerases that activate RNA turnover and quality control pathways by targeting aberrant and short-lived RNA substrates to the nuclear exosome for degradation [1], [4]-[7],[15],[20]. Trf4 and trf5 are synthetically lethal and depletion of Trf5p strengthens the defects in RNA maturation of trf4Delta mutants, suggesting that Trf4p and Trf5p have partially overlapping functions in vivo[6],[7],[20]. To globally investigate the extent of functional redundancy and to systematically identify Trf4p- and Trf5p-specific RNA targets, we used microarrays to compare RNA expression profiles of S. cerevisiae mutant strains lacking Trf4p or Trf5p with that of WT cells (Figure 1, Table S1). We found that almost all (>90%) of the 715 features that were at least 2-fold changed, were selectively increased in either the trf4Delta or the trf5Delta mutants. This finding is in agreement with known functions of these proteins in RNA degradation and their depletion is therefore expected to lead to the accumulation of RNA targets [1], [5]-[7],[20]. However, in contrast to the proposed functional redundancy of Trf4p and Trf5p, we found that trf4 and trf5 deletion affected barely overlapping sets of transcripts (Figure 1A). Such heterogeneity of the genes with altered expression was previously reported for different mutants of the exosome complex, possibly reflecting differential target specificities by the different subunits of the complex [16].
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 19 28 19 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 37 46 33 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 220 229 212 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 234 243 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 388 392 372 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Neil1">[18]</xref>
###xml 393 397 377 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Xu1">[19]</xref>
###xml 550 553 534 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
###xml 561 569 545 553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 571 580 555 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 582 586 566 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Camblong1">[29]</xref>
###xml 587 591 571 575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Uhler1">[45]</xref>
###xml 824 827 808 811 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>
###xml 834 838 818 822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Camblong1">[29]</xref>
###xml 935 942 919 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Interestingly, the trf4Delta and the trf5Delta mutants differed in the number of ncRNAs that accumulated in the cell. NcRNAs represented 17% and 4% of the transcripts that were selectively increased (>2-fold, FDR<5%) in trf4Delta and trf5Delta mutants, respectively. However, our microarrays cover only a fraction of the experimentally defined CUTs derived from intergenic regions (IGRs) [18],[19]. Moreover, functional antisense RNAs are also not detected with our oligo arrays including the antisense RNAs spanning the promoter region of different PHO genes (Figure 6, Figure S5) [29],[45]. Nevertheless, application of qRT-PCR with antisense-RNA specific primers suggests that both TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 complexes as well as the exosome participate in RNA-mediated regulatory mechanisms to modulate the expression of several PHO genes [29] but that only TRAMP4 triggers the exosome-mediated degradation of regulatory antisense PHO RNAs in vivo.
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 51 54 51 54 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 56 59 56 59 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 61 65 61 65 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Davis1">[14]</xref>
###xml 66 70 66 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houalla1">[16]</xref>
###xml 241 248 241 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 454 457 454 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova1">[1]</xref>
###xml 458 461 458 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 462 465 462 465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 610 613 610 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 614 617 614 617 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Dez1">[8]</xref>
###xml 618 622 618 622 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
In conclusion and consistent with previous reports [6], [7], [14]-[16], our experiments support a major role for Trf4p in the exosome-mediated degradation of ncRNAs and suggest that TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 may function on specific subsets of RNAs in vivo. However, it remains to be further investigated how the TRAMP4 and the TRAMP5 complexes achieve specificity for their selective targets. TRAMP4 and TRAMP5 consist of structurally similar protein complexes [1],[5],[7], therefore specificity could be conferred by protein-protein interactions that are engaged by Trf4p or Trf5p and by the Air1p or Air2p subunits [5]-[8],[20]. Misfolding of the RNPs or the association of proteins with aberrant RNAs may act as selectivity factors that eventually favor the recruitment of either TRAMP4 or TRAMP5 to the RNP target.
###end p 59
###begin title 60
The Polyadenylation Activity of Trf4p Promotes Degradation of a Subset of RNAs
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 156 163 156 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 168 176 168 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 176 179 176 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Kadaba1">[4]</xref>
###xml 180 183 180 183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 312 321 312 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 329 338 325 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 354 357 346 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 358 361 350 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 362 366 354 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Davis1">[14]</xref>
###xml 367 371 359 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Egecioglu1">[15]</xref>
###xml 372 376 364 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley3">[20]</xref>
###xml 487 495 479 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 626 629 618 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Rougemaille1">[9]</xref>
###xml 630 634 622 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 674 678 666 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 716 720 708 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 725 729 717 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 745 748 737 740 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1188 1197 1180 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1226 1234 1214 1222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1236 1244 1224 1232 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1400 1409 1388 1393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1695 1699 1679 1683 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Bernstein1">[46]</xref>
###xml 1868 1877 1852 1857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1912 1921 1892 1901 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s001">Figure S1</xref>
Several groups have previously demonstrated that the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p stimulates the exosome-mediated degradation of different RNA species in vivo and in vitro[4]-[6]. Consistently, rRNA processing intermediates, snRNAs, snoRNAs, and a few CUTs accumulate as non-polyadenylated molecules in the trf4Delta or the trf5Delta mutant strains [6],[7],[14],[15],[20]. Intriguingly, even though polyadenylation activity is required for the degradation of highly structured RNAs in vitro, it was reported that a polyadenylation-defective form of Trf4p (Trf4p-DADA) can also activate degradation of RNAs by the exosome [9],[30]. Moreover, a polyadenylation-defective trf4 mutation can rescue the lethality of trf4 and trf5 double mutants [7]. These findings lead to a model, which proposes that the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p may not generally be necessary to guide RNA to the exosome for degradation. However, the universality of this model and whether there might be sets of RNAs that differentially depend on polyadenylation activity has not been addressed so far. Surprisingly, we found that Trf4p-DADA almost fully suppressed the altered gene expression profile of the trf4Delta mutant upon overexpression (Figure 1, Table S1). This finding generally supports and extends the model introduced above: Since Trf4p-DADA only partially rescues the accumulation of selected RNAs in the trf4Delta mutant, we suggest that the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p enhances the degradation of most target RNAs by the exosome, but this function is not essential. Polyadenylation in combination with the helicase activity of Mtr4p, which has a marked preference for binding to poly(A) RNAs [46], may be required for digestion of highly structured RNAs. This may be exemplified by the higher fraction of non-coding RNAs among the RNAs that remained accumulated in trf4Delta mutants overexpressing TRF4-DADA (Figure S1).
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 70 74 70 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 399 403 399 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 437 445 437 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4-236</italic>
###xml 533 536 533 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-LaCava1">[6]</xref>
###xml 616 625 616 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 707 716 707 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4 trf5</italic>
###xml 732 735 732 735 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wyers1">[7]</xref>
However, additional mechanisms may account for the suppression of the trf4 mutation by Trf4p-DADA. For instance, since the TRAMP complexes share common subunits, an intriguing speculation is that Trf4p-DADA, in the context of TRAMP4, recruits Trf5p to target RNAs. Trf5p then adds poly(A) tails to facilitate exosome-mediated degradation. In agreement with this idea is the finding that deletion of trf5 in the polyadenylation-defective trf4-236 mutant enhanced the defect in the degradation of CUTs compared to either single mutant [6]. Although this model could explain some of the observed effects in our system (Figure 2D), it cannot account for the observation that Trf4p-DADA rescues the lethality of trf4 trf5 double mutants [7].
###end p 62
###begin title 63
Trf4p and Trf5p Stimulate the Degradation of Introns
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 135 139 135 139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-DaninKreiselman1">[38]</xref>
###xml 140 144 140 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Khalid1">[39]</xref>
###xml 145 149 145 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Pandit1">[47]</xref>
###xml 286 293 286 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 295 303 295 303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 487 495 487 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 497 506 497 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 667 676 667 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 680 689 676 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 786 795 778 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4 trf5</italic>
Whereas the mechanism of splicing has been extensively investigated, very little is known about the degradation of spliced-out introns [38],[39],[47]. In this work, we showed by combined crosslinking-RNA-immunopurification experiments that TRAMP4 likely interacts directly with introns in vivo (Figure 3). We also provide experimental evidence supporting a role for TRAMP4 in the degradation of spliced-out introns, which is largely independent of the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p (Figure 2, Figure S4). However, we could not find a simple correlation between the introns that were highly associated with TRAMP4, and the relative changes of expression in single trf4Delta or trf5Delta mutants. Moreover, because the expression levels of some introns became exclusively affected in trf4 trf5 double mutants, Trf5p may promote the breakdown of introns in the absence of Trf4p suggesting functional redundancy between Trf4p and Trf5p in intron decay. Further experiments are required to unravel the contributions of different TRAMP complexes in intron decay and to delineate the exact extent of functional redundancy.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 583 587 583 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-DaninKreiselman1">[38]</xref>
We envisage that after splicing, intron lariats are rapidly converted into linear forms by the debranching enzyme Dbr1p. Subsets of specific linear introns are then captured by TRAMP complexes to be eventually degraded by the nuclear exosome. Additional pathways may also exist, which involve the 5' to 3' exoribonuclease Rat1 and the endonuclease RNaseIII. In fact, lariats that contain RNaseIII binding sites can also undergo internal cleavage by RNaseIII irrespective of the Dbr1-mediated debranching, generating cleavage products that are eventually degraded by exoribonucleases [38].
###end p 65
###begin title 66
Trf4p Functions in Subtelomeric RNA Silencing and Telomere Maintenance
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 75 88 75 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 93 101 93 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 133 137 133 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 138 142 138 142 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vasiljeva1">[48]</xref>
###xml 306 315 306 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 320 329 316 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 364 373 356 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 381 389 369 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 391 400 379 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 510 519 498 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 842 846 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Dror1">[49]</xref>
###xml 847 851 835 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Moazed1">[50]</xref>
###xml 894 898 882 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Dror1">[49]</xref>
###xml 899 903 887 891 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Moazed1">[50]</xref>
###xml 1023 1027 1011 1015 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley4">[23]</xref>
###xml 75 88 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 93 101 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
Transcription at heterochromatin regions was recently reported to occur in S. cerevisiae and S. pombe cells that lack Trf4p or Rrp6p [30],[48]. Consistent with these reports, we detected the accumulation of a number of RNAs originating from silent mating type cassettes and subtelomeric transcripts in the trf4Delta and rrp6Delta mutants, and to a lower extent in trf5Delta cells (Figure 5, Figure S5). This activity is partially dependent on the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p and on a functional exosome (Figure 4B). Although further experiments are needed to elucidate how Trf4p and the exosome contribute to the silencing of heterochromatin domains, we hypothesize that during degradation of subtelomeric RNAs, TRAMP4, and the exosome modulate the interaction or the accessibility of chromatin remodeling factors such as Sir2 and Set1 [49],[50] within sites of heterochromatin formation [49],[50]. There is a growing body of evidence that suggests interactions of Trf4p and chromatin remodeling factors (reviewed in [23]).
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 91 104 91 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 109 117 109 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 258 262 258 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 263 267 263 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Wang2">[31]</xref>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Azzalin1">[51]</xref>
###xml 411 415 411 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Luke1">[41]</xref>
###xml 467 471 467 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 496 505 496 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 516 529 512 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 623 632 619 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 641 650 633 642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 723 727 715 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Houseley5">[30]</xref>
###xml 818 827 810 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 1064 1073 1056 1061 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1304 1313 1292 1297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1448 1452 1432 1436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1541 1545 1525 1529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1654 1658 1638 1642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6</italic>
###xml 1660 1664 1644 1648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1701 1705 1685 1689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 1733 1737 1717 1721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST1</italic>
###xml 1739 1743 1723 1727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST2</italic>
###xml 1749 1753 1733 1737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EST3</italic>
###xml 1998 2002 1982 1986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 2002 2006 1986 1990 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Peterson1">[42]</xref>
###xml 2028 2032 2012 2016 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLC1</italic>
###xml 2040 2049 2024 2029 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 91 104 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 109 117 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 405 410 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 516 529 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Transcription of heterochromatin regions can regulate important physiological pathways. In S. cerevisiae and S. pombe strains with mutations in TRAMP or exosome components, accumulation of heterochromatic CUTs has been linked to changes in rDNA copy numbers [30],[31]. Likewise, high levels of telomeric repeat-containing RNAs (TERRA) were shown to act in telomere maintenance in mammalian cells [51] and yeast [41]. In addition to alteration in the rDNA copy number [30], we discovered that the trf4Delta mutant of S. cerevisiae exhibits a severe shortening of telomeres and that telomeres were only mildly reduced in the rrp6Delta mutant (Figure 5A). Similarly to what was reported for the regulation of the rDNA repeats [30], telomere maintenance was not strictly dependent on the polyadenylation activity of Trf4 (Figure 5B). Although accumulation of subtelomeric RNAs may perturb the chromatin integrity at the telomeres and negatively affect the telomerase activity, additional mechanisms probably account for the severe shortening of chromosome ends in the trf4Delta mutant. In fact, our results do not provide any straight evidence of a direct link between the extent of subtelomeric RNA accumulation and the severity of telomere shortening. Rather it emerged that the telomeric phenotype of the trf4Delta mutant can in part reflect imbalances in the expression level between the protein subunits Est1p, Est2p, Est3p, and the RNA component TLC1 of the telomerase. We propose that Trf4p stimulates the exosome-mediated degradation of TLC1 through a polyadenylation-independent mechanism. However, in contrast to what happens in cells defective in rrp6, trf4 deletion causes only high levels of TLC1, whereas the expression of EST1, EST2, and EST3 remains unchanged. It was previously demonstrated that recruitment of the telomerase holoenzyme is mediated by the heterodimeric Ku70/80 complex, which binds the chromosome ends and interacts with the telomerase via a small stem loop region of TLC1[42]. Thus, the excess of TLC1 in the trf4Delta mutant could interfere with the recruitment of the telomerase at the chromosome ends and ultimately lead to telomere shortening.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 253 261 253 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g007">Figure 7</xref>
To conclude, in this work we provide experimental evidence demonstrating that in addition to RNA surveillance, Trf4p and Trf5p participate in post-transcriptional regulatory networks that connect RNA degradation with DNA metabolism and gene regulation (Figure 7). Although the polyadenylation activity of Trf4p clearly enhances the efficiency of degradation of a broad variety of RNAs via the TRAMP4/exosome complex, expression of the Trf4 protein rather than its polyadenylation activity emerged to be essential for the maintenance of effective post-transcriptional regulatory pathways in the cell.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
Combined view on the current knowledge of the different roles of the TRAMP4 complex.
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PHO</italic>

###end p 71
