###end title 72
###begin title 73
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Yeast Strains and Plasmid Construction
###end title 73
###begin p 74
###xml 17 30 17 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 448 456 436 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s011">Table S5</xref>
###xml 462 471 450 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 476 485 460 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 557 561 537 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 570 574 550 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6</italic>
###xml 590 596 570 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">kanMX6</italic>
###xml 711 715 691 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FPR1</italic>
###xml 717 724 697 704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YNL135C</italic>
###xml 839 848 819 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 895 899 871 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 927 933 903 909 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">natMX4</italic>
###xml 992 996 968 972 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Goldstein1">[52]</xref>
###xml 17 30 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 106 111 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 156 161 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 242 247 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 417 422 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Manipulations of S. cerevisiae strains were performed by standard procedures. Cells were grown in YPD (1% yeast extract, 2% peptone, 2% glucose), YPGal (1% yeast extract, 2% peptone, 2% galactose), or in synthetic minimal medium (0.67% Bacto-yeast nitrogen base without amino acid, 2% glucose, and amino acid supplements as required) at 30degreesC. Temperature shifts to 37degreesC were done in a shaking water bath. Yeast strains are described in Table S5. The trf5Delta and rrp6Delta mutant strains were purchased from Open Biosystems. Replacement of the trf5 and the rrp6 genes with the kanMX6 cassette was confirmed by PCR following the manufacturer's instructions. The strain with C-terminal TAP-fusion of FPR1 (YNL135C) was purchased from BioCat (Heidelberg, Germany). The correct integration of the TAP-tag was verified by PCR. The trf4Delta strain is a derivative of BY4741 in which the trf4 gene was replaced with the natMX4 marker by homologous recombination as previously reported [52]; primer sequences can be provided upon request.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 14 23 14 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 53 57 49 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 79 83 75 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 107 120 103 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 172 178 168 174 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CCCGGG</underline>
###xml 167 205 163 201 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-GT<underline>CCCGGG</underline>AAATATGGGGGCAAAGAGTGTAAC-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 231 237 227 233 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GTCGAC</underline>
###xml 226 265 222 261 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AC<underline>GTCGAC</underline>TTATTAAAGGGTATAAGGATTATAT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 485 496 481 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pNOP1::TRF4</italic>
###xml 499 508 495 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 548 559 540 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pNOP1::TRF4</italic>
###xml 728 737 714 719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 863 872 845 850 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 107 120 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
To complement trf4Delta with the wild type allele of trf4 the coding region of trf4 was PCR amplified from S. cerevisiae BY4741 genomic DNA with primers XmaI-trf4-Fw (5'-GTCCCGGGAAATATGGGGGCAAAGAGTGTAAC-3') and trf4-Rev-SalI (5'-ACGTCGACTTATTAAAGGGTATAAGGATTATAT-3') (restriction sites are underlined). The insert was cloned in pGEMT-easy vector (Promega), digested with XmaI and SalI restriction enzymes and ligated into the same sites on the pNOPPATA1L vector to generate pNOPPATA1L(pNOP1::TRF4). Trf4Delta cells were transformed with pNOPPATA1L(pNOP1::TRF4) and transformants were selected for leucine prototrophy in synthetic medium at 30degreesC. The correct integration of the fragment was verified by sequencing. Control trf4Delta/pNOPPAT1L and BY4741/ pNOPPATA1L strains were selected for leucine prototrophy onto synthetic medium after transformation of trf4Delta and BY4741 cells with the pNOPPAT1L plasmid.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 11 15 11 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 79 83 79 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 88 92 88 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5</italic>
###xml 117 130 117 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 182 188 182 188 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAGCTC</underline>
###xml 177 215 177 215 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-GT<underline>GAGCTC</underline>AAATATGGGGGCAAAGAGTGTAAC-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 240 246 240 246 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CTCGAG</underline>
###xml 236 274 236 274 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;AC<underline>CTCGAG</underline>TTATTAAAGGGTATAAGGATTATAT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 299 305 299 305 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GGATCC</underline>
###xml 294 335 294 335 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AA<underline>GGATCC</underline>CATAATGACAAGGCTCAAAGCAAAATA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 356 395 356 395 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AGCTCGAGTTATTAAAGAGCCTGGCCTTTAGAG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 462 465 462 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sac</italic>
###xml 467 470 467 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 480 484 480 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BamH</italic>
###xml 486 489 486 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 566 577 566 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pGAL1::TRF4</italic>
###xml 589 600 589 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pGAL1::TRF5</italic>
###xml 617 636 617 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 678 682 670 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 697 701 689 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 909 913 891 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1184 1188 1152 1156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4</italic>
###xml 1233 1236 1201 1204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sac</italic>
###xml 1238 1241 1206 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 1251 1255 1219 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BamH</italic>
###xml 1257 1260 1225 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 117 130 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
To express trf4 or trf5 from an inducible pGAL1 promoter the coding regions of trf4 and trf5 were PCR amplified from S. cerevisiae BY4741 genomic DNA with primers SacI-trf4-Fw (5'-GTGAGCTCAAATATGGGGGCAAAGAGTGTAAC-3') and trf4-Rev-XhoI (5'ACCTCGAGTTATTAAAGGGTATAAGGATTATAT-3') or BamHI-trf5-Fw (5'-AAGGATCCCATAATGACAAGGCTCAAAGCAAAATA-3') and trf5-Rev-XhoI (5'-AGCTCGAGTTATTAAAGAGCCTGGCCTTTAGAG-3'). The fragments were cloned into pGEMT-easy vector, digested with SacI-XhoI or with BamHI-XhoI and ligated into the same sites of pYC6/CT (Invitrogen) to generate pSAL1 (pGAL1::TRF4) or pSAL2 (pGAL1::TRF5), respectively. trf4Delta trf5Delta mutant cells complemented with wild type TRF4 by the pRS416-TRF4 plasmid were successively transformed with either pSAL1 or pSAL2. Transformants were selected onto YPD supplemented with blasticidin (InvivoGen) 150 microg/ml at 30degreesC. To induce the loss of the pRS416-TRF4 plasmid, blasticidin resistant colonies were inoculated three times on synthetic medium supplemented with 2% galactose, blasticidin (15 microg/ml) and 5-fluoro-orotic acid (1 microg/ml; Zymo Research) at 30degreesC. Transformation with pSAL1 or pSAL2 and loss of pRS416-TRF4 was confirmed by restriction digestion with SacI-XhoI or with BamHI-XhoI of plasmid DNA preparations purified from clones that were uracil auxotrophic, blasticidin resistant, and glucose sensitive.
###end p 76
###begin title 77
RNA Purification
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 322 325 308 311 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 417 420 397 400 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 70 75 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Total RNA was extracted with the hot phenol extraction method. Single yeast colonies were inoculated in 5 ml YPD or YPGal medium supplemented with the appropriate amount of selective drug (G418, 200 microg/ml; clonNat, 100 microg/ml) and incubated overnight at 30degreesC (pre-cultures). Pre-cultures were diluted to an OD600 of 0.1 in 50 ml of fresh YPD or YPGal medium without drugs and grown at 30degreesC to an OD600 of 0.7. Cells were collected by centrifugation for 5 min at 3,000 g and resuspended in AE buffer (50 mM Na-acetate, 10 mM EDTA, pH 5.3) with 1% SDS. After adding one volume of phenol (pH 5.3), the suspension was vigorously shaken for 1 min and incubated at 65degreesC for 4 min in a heating block (Thermomixer comfort, Eppendorf). The aqueous phase was separated from the phenol phase by centrifugation at 20,000 g and extracted again with phenol (pH 5.3) and then with chloroform. Total RNA was precipitated from the aqueous phase by the addition of 2.6 volumes of ice-cold ethanol and of 1/10 volume of 1 M Na-acetate (pH 5.3) for 20 min on ice. The precipitated RNA was recovered by centrifugation at 20,000 g for 30 min at 4degreesC, the pellet was washed with 70% ethanol and resuspended in DEPC-treated water.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 68 72 68 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">free</italic>
###xml 348 351 339 342 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">260</sub>
To remove contaminating DNA, RNA preparations were treated with DNA-freetrade mark (Ambion) according to the manufacturer's instructions. The integrity of RNA samples was routinely checked by gel electrophoresis (1.2% agarose - 6% formaldehyde) in 1x HEPES buffer (50 mM HEPES [pH 7.8], 10 mM EDTA) and RNA was quantified by UV-spectrophotometry (A260) with a Nanodrop device (Witeg AG).
###end p 79
###begin title 80
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In Vivo</italic>
In Vivo Depletion of Trf4 or Trf5 Proteins
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 23 43 23 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916; trf5&#916;/</italic>
###xml 59 63 51 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 69 79 57 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;/</italic>
###xml 280 283 254 257 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 355 358 323 326 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 596 597 558 559 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 595 597 557 559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t<sub>0</sub></italic>
###xml 684 685 640 641 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 683 685 639 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t<sub>1</sub></italic>
###xml 779 780 729 730 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 778 780 728 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t<sub>1</sub></italic>
Single colonies of the trf4Delta trf5Delta/pSAL1 or of the trf4Delta trf5Delta/pSAL2 mutant strains were inoculated in YPGal liquid medium supplemented with blasticidin (150 microg/ml; InvivoGen) at 30degreesC and grown overnight. The following day, cultures were diluted to an OD600 of 0.1 in 300 ml of fresh YPGal medium and grown at 30degreesC to an OD600 of 0.7. Cultures were equally split into three tubes and cells were collected by centrifugation at RT for 5 min at 3,000 g. After centrifugation, one-third of the culture was rapidly frozen in liquid nitrogen and stored at -70degreesC (t0 time point); one-third was resuspended in YPGal and incubated at 30degreesC for 1 h (t1 Gal time point), while the rest of the culture was inoculated in YPD at 30degreesC for 1 h (t1 Glc time point). Cells were collected by centrifugation and stored at -70degreesC. Total RNA was purified from the cell pellet as described above.
###end p 81
###begin title 82
Microarray Analysis
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 118 131 118 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 135 136 135 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</italic>
###xml 118 131 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 146 151 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
DNA microarrays contained 10,944 oligo probes (70-mers) from the Array-Ready Oligo Set Version 1.1 representing 6,388 S. cerevisiae ORFs, and the Yeast Brown Lab Oligo Extension Version (YBOX vers. 1.0) with 3,456 probes to detect ncRNAs, rRNA precursors, introns, exon-intron and exon-exon junctions, other sequences predicted to be expressed, additional probes for genes with high cross-hybridization potential and controls for array quality measurements and normalization. Details of oligonucleotide selection and probe sequences are available from the Operon website (). All microarray data are available at the Stanford Microarray Database (SMD) or at the Gene Expression Omnibus (GEO) with accession number GSE16107.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
The probes were printed on epoxy coated glass slides (Nexterion slide E) at the Center for Integrative Genomics, University of Lausanne, Switzerland. Oligo arrays were blocked in 5x SSC, 0.1 mg/ ml BSA, 0.1% SDS for 1 h at 42degreesC, and subsequently washed three times in 0.1x SSC for 5 min at RT, rinsed in water for 30 s, and dried by centrifugation (500 g for 2 min). The slides were used the same day.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 661 662 647 648 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 2139 2148 2109 2114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 2150 2159 2116 2121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 2164 2173 2126 2131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 2174 2183 2132 2141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 2321 2322 2279 2280 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 2493 2503 2451 2461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s013">Dataset S1</xref>
###xml 2608 2612 2566 2570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Buhler1">[28]</xref>
###xml 2708 2709 2666 2667 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
###xml 2806 2810 2764 2768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Baldi1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1075 1078 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">Cat</span>
###xml 1195 1200 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Microarray analysis was performed by competitive hybridization of Cy3 and Cy5 fluorescently labeled cDNA. Total RNA (25 microg) was reverse transcribed with SuperScript RT II (Invitrogen) in the presence of 2.5 mM aminoallyl-dUTP (Sigma) and dNTPs, with a 1:1 mixture of dT20V and random nonamer (N9) primers (5 microg of each, Sigma). After first strand cDNA synthesis, RNA was hydrolyzed with 0.1 M NaOH and 0.1 M EDTA at 65degreesC for 15 min, and samples were neutralized with 0.35 M HEPES (pH 8.0). Clean up of the reaction mix was performed in Microcon-YM30 (Millipore) filled with distilled water. Amino-allyl containing cDNA was eluted with 100 mM NaHCO3 (pH 9.0) and covalently linked to either fluorescent Cy3 or Cy5 NHS-monoester (GE Healthcare). Thereby, cDNAs derived from wild-type control cells were labeled with Cy3, the ones derived from mutant cells with Cy5. Unincorporated dyes were removed with the QIAquick PCR Purification Kit (Qiagen). The samples were mixed in standard formamide based hybridization buffer (Ocimum Biosolution Hybridzation Solution, Cat. No. 1180-000010) supplemented with 1 mg/ml poly(A) in a final volume of 20 microl, and competitively hybridized to yeast oligo arrays in a sealed hybridization chamber (Corning) at 42degreesC for 12-16 h. Arrays were successively washed in three buffer chambers filled with 2x SSC (300 mM NaCl, 30 mM Na-citrate, pH 7.0), 0.2% SDS; 2x SSC; and 0.2x SSC. The first wash was performed at 42degreesC for 12 min, the subsequent washes at RT for 12 min. After briefly rinsing in ethanol, microarrays were scanned with an Axon Instruments Scanner 4200A (Molecular Devices). Scanning parameters were adjusted to give similar fluorescent intensities in both channels. Data were collected with GenePix Pro 5.1 (Molecular Devices) and spots with abnormal morphology were excluded from further analysis. Array data were exported to Acuity 4.0 (Molecular Devices) and normalized to the mean of ratio of medians = 1 excluding the signals from control features. We collected three biological replicates each for determining the relative changes of transcript levels in the trf4Delta, trf5Delta and trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutant cells compared to the respective wild-type cells (total of 9 arrays). Data were filtered in Acuity for regression correlation (Rgn2>0.5), signal to noise ratio >2.5 in both channels, and only features that met these criteria in >60% of arrays were considered for further analysis (total 7481 features; Dataset S1). Data were exported into Microsoft Excel to determine percentile ranks and to perform SAM (version 3.0 [28]). We used the web interface for Cyber-T () to employ statistical analyses based on regularized t-tests that use a Bayesian estimate of the variance among gene measurements within an experiment [34].
###end p 85
###begin p 86
###xml 130 139 130 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 141 150 137 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 155 174 147 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 201 209 189 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s007">Table S1</xref>
###xml 310 314 298 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Eisen1">[53]</xref>
###xml 382 386 370 374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Saldanha1">[54]</xref>
###xml 388 397 376 385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 601 602 589 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
The 715 unique features (9.5% of all analyzed features) that were on average at least 2-fold changed with an FDR<5% in either the trf4Delta, trf5Delta, or trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA replicates were compiled (Table S1). The genes and arrays were hierarchically clustered based on Pearson correlations with Cluster 3.0 [53] and the result was visualized as a heatmap with Java TreeView 1.0. [54] (Figure 1A). Commonly enriched GO terms among list of genes were retrieved with GO Term Finder that uses a hypergeometric distribution with Multiple Hypothesis Correction (i.e., Bonferroni Correction) to calculate p-values (SGD; ).
###end p 86
###begin title 87
Quantitative Real-Time PCR
###end title 87
###begin p 88
###xml 275 277 267 269 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">20</sub>
###xml 930 931 894 895 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1004 1008 968 972 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Pfaffl1">[55]</xref>
###xml 1171 1179 1135 1143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s012">Table S6</xref>
qRT-PCR was performed with an ABI Prism 7000 Sequence Detection System (ABI Prism) and the Power SYBR Green PCR Master Mix (Applied Biosystems) according to the manufacturer's instructions. The first strand cDNA was synthesized with 5 microg of total RNA, 50 microM oligo(dT)20, 0.1 microM random hexamers and SuperScript RT III (Invitrogen). RNA was subsequently hydrolyzed with 125 mM NaOH and 10 mM EDTA at 65degreesC for 15 min. The mix was neutralized with 400 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0) and loaded onto a Microcon-YM30 (Millipore) concentrator column filled with 10 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0). After centrifugation for 8 min at 13,500 g the microcon was filled again with 10 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0). This step was repeated twice. After elution, the cDNA was used as template for PCR with the following conditions: 95degreesC for 10 min; 40 cycles at 95degreesC for 15 s, and 60degreesC for 1 min. Transcript abundance was calculated as log2 of normalized ratios with the Pfaffel method of relative quantification [55]. Data were normalized to actin mRNA levels. (All primers used for quantitative real time PCR analysis and for strand specific reverse transcription are listed in Table S6.) Primer sequences for the strand specific synthesis of the antisense-Ty1 (RTL) cDNA and of the antisense-PHO5, -PHO11, and -PHO89 cDNAs can be provided upon request.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In Vivo</italic>
In Vivo Cross-Linking and Ribonucleoprotein-Immunopurification-Chip Analysis (X-RIP-Chip)
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 87 90 87 90 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 147 150 141 144 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 689 690 677 678 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 72 77 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
1 L of fresh YPD medium was inoculated with an overnight pre-culture of yeast cells (OD600 = 0.1) that were further cultured at 30degreesC to an OD600 = 0.7. RNAs and proteins were cross-linked with 1% formaldehyde that was added directly to the culture for 7 min at RT. The cross-linking reaction was subsequently quenched by the addition of 125 mM glycine (pH 7.0) for 5 min at RT. During cross-linking and quenching reactions the cultures were maintained under constant shaking at 100 rpm. Cells were harvested by centrifugation (1,500 g) at 4degreesC, washed twice with 50 ml of ice-cold PBS, and lysed in 5 ml of ice-cold lysis buffer (20 mM Tris-HCl [pH 7.5], 140 mM KCl, 1.8 mM MgCl2, 0.1% NP-40, 0.1 mM DTT, 10% glycerol, 0.2 mg/ml heparin, 0.5 microg/ml Leupeptin, 0.8 microg/ml Pepstatin, 50 U/ml SUPERaseIn [Amersham]) by grinding in mortar filled with liquid nitrogen. Contaminating DNA was digested with 20 U/ml RNAse-free DNase I (Promega). The WCE was centrifuged twice at 13,000 g for 10 min at 4degreesC to remove cell debris. The protein concentration of the extract was determined with the Bradford method (Bio-Rad Protein Assay, BioRad). To purify total RNA from extracts for microarray analysis (input RNA sample), 100 microl of WCE was digested with Proteinase K (0.4 mg/ml) for 30 min at 37degreesC, heated up to 70degreesC for 45 min to reverse the formaldehyde cross-linking, and proteins were extracted with phenol-chloroform-isoamyl alcohol (PCI, 25:24:1). RNA was precipitated with 1.5 M LiCl at -20degreesC overnight and collected by 30 min centrifugation (14,000 g) at 4degreesC. The RNA pellet was washed twice with 70% ethanol and resuspended in DEPC-treated water.
###end p 90
###begin p 91
###xml 83 89 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Cross-linked TAP-tagged proteins were captured from the WCE as follows: 300 microl rabbit IgG-coupled agarose beads (Sigma) were equilibrated at 4degreesC in lysis buffer supplemented with 5% BSA. WCE was added to the blocked IgG beads and mixed on a rotator overnight at 4degreesC. TAP-tagged proteins were then recovered by spinning down the IgG beads at 72 g for 2 min at 4degreesC. Beads were thoroughly washed three times with ice-cold lysis buffer supplemented with increasing concentrations of NaCl (100 mM, 200 mM, and 350 mM). RNP complexes were digested in 1 ml of elution buffer (50 mM Tris-HCl [pH 7.0], 1% SDS, 5 mM EDTA, 10 mM DTT, 140 mM KCl, 5% glycerol, 0.01% NP-40) with 100 microl Proteinase K (4 mg/ml) for 20 min at 37degreesC. Formaldehyde cross-linking was reversed by incubation of the eluate at 70degreesC for 45 min in a gently shaken heating block. Immunopurified RNA (IP-RNA) was isolated by extraction with PCI and isopropanol precipitation. The RNA pellet was washed twice with 70% ethanol and resuspended in DEPC-water.
###end p 91
###begin p 92
###xml 589 590 585 586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 643 653 639 649 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000555.s014">Dataset S2</xref>
###xml 217 222 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
For the microarray analysis of the IP-RNA, 5 microg of total RNA (input RNA) and 500 ng of IP-RNA were converted into Cy3 and Cy5 fluorescently labeled cDNA, respectively, and samples were competitively hybridized on yeast oligo arrays as described above. We collected data from three biological replicates with Trf4-TAP, from two replicates with Fpr1-TAP and from one untagged control (BY4741 strain) sample. Array data were filtered in Acuity for signal to noise ratio >3 for the channel with the input RNA (Cy3), and percentile ranks for filtered data were calculated based upon the log2 of the Cy5/Cy3 ratio in each experiment with Excel (Dataset S2).
###end p 92
###begin title 93
Northern Blot Analysis
###end title 93
###begin p 94
###xml 69 73 69 73 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Dichtl1">[56]</xref>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Garas1">[57]</xref>
Northern blotting experiments were performed as previously described [56],[57]. Briefly, 35 microg of total RNA in RNA loading buffer (50% formamide, 6% formaldehyde, 50 mM HEPES [pH 7.8], 0.25% xylene cyanol, 0.25% bromophenol blue, 10% glycerol) was loaded on a 1.5% agarose-6% formaldehyde gel and fractionated in 1x HEPES buffer (50 mM HEPES [pH 7.8]; 10 mM EDTA) at 50-60 Volts for 15 h. After washing of the gel in distilled water for 15 min, the RNA was partially cleaved with 75 mM NaOH for 15 min. The gel was neutralized in a solution comprised of 5 M Tris-HCl (pH 7.0) and 1.5 M NaCl for 15 min, and equilibrated in 10x SSC for 20 min. Capillary transfer of the RNA to Hybond-N+ membranes (Amersham) was performed in 10x SSC over night. RNA was UV-crosslinked to the membrane in a UV Stratalinker 1800 (Stratagene) with 1200 microJ.
###end p 94
###begin p 95
###xml 77 79 73 75 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 157 159 149 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 357 393 349 385 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AGAAATGGTATGTTAAAAAGTGCTCAGATG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 415 443 407 435 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CAGCGTCAGACTGAGAAAAAAC-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 462 496 454 488 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CGCATAATTATGGCAAATGTTATGAAGG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 517 550 509 542 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CGAATAACTCTACCTGTTTAAATGAGG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 566 572 558 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS24A</italic>
###xml 577 582 569 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL2B</italic>
###xml 623 654 615 646 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-TCTGACGCTGTTACTATCCGTACTA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 675 705 667 697 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AATCGGCGTTACGACGAGCAACCT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 723 753 715 745 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CACACCAGATTAAGACAAGGTGCT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 773 805 765 797 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-GAACCACGTAGTAAACCGGTTCTTCT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 821 827 813 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPS24A</italic>
###xml 831 836 823 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPL2B</italic>
###xml 905 909 897 901 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK1</italic>
###xml 941 945 933 937 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Dichtl1">[56]</xref>
###xml 1075 1076 1067 1068 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1078 1079 1070 1071 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
DNA probes for hybridization were prepared by random incorporation of alpha-[32P] dATP with the Random Prime DNA Labeling Kit (Roche). Unincorporated alpha-[32P] dATP was removed by MicroSpinTM G-25 Columns (GE Healthcare). DNA templates for the preparation of the randomly labeled probes were produced by PCR amplification with primer pairs rps24A-int-Fw (5'-AGAAATGGTATGTTAAAAAGTGCTCAGATG-3') and rps24A-int-Rev (5'-CAGCGTCAGACTGAGAAAAAAC-3') or rpl2B-int-Fw (5'-CGCATAATTATGGCAAATGTTATGAAGG-3') and rpl2B-int-Rev (5'-CGAATAACTCTACCTGTTTAAATGAGG-3') to detect the RPS24A and RPL2B introns, and primer pairs rps24A-ex-Fw (5'-TCTGACGCTGTTACTATCCGTACTA-3') and rps24A-ex-Rev (5'-AATCGGCGTTACGACGAGCAACCT-3') or rpl2B-ex-Fw (5'-CACACCAGATTAAGACAAGGTGCT-3') and rpl2B-ex-Rev (5'-GAACCACGTAGTAAACCGGTTCTTCT-3') to detect the RPS24A or RPL2B mRNAs. The DNA template for the preparation of the randomly labeled PGK1 probe was previously described [56]. Hybridization was carried out in rolling tubes in hybridization buffer containing 50% formamide, 5x SSPE (750 mM NaCl, 50 mM NaH2PO4, 5 mM EDTA, pH 7.4), 5x Denhardts solution, 1% SDS, and 200 microg/ml salmon sperm DNA according to standard procedures. The result of the hybridization was visualized with a Phosphor Imager.
###end p 95
###begin title 96
Western and Dot Blot Analysis of Immunopurified Protein Complexes
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 343 346 339 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 506 522 502 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 593 594 589 590 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 731 733 727 729 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 795 798 791 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Vanacova2">[5]</xref>
###xml 506 534 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">Escherichia coli strain BL21</span>
###xml 970 976 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1013 1018 <span type="species:ncbi:9823">swine</span>
###xml 1024 1030 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Two microl of protein samples were directly spotted onto the nitrocellulose membrane (Whatman) for dot blot analysis. For Western blots, proteins were separated on 12% polyacrylamide gels, transferred to nitrocellulose membranes, and incubated with antibodies indicated in the figure legends. The anti-TAP antibodies were previously described [5]. To generate anti-Air2 antibodies a C-terminal fragment of Air2p (comprising amino acids 210-344 of Air2p) was cloned in pET22b (Novagen) and expressed in the Escherichia coli strain BL21. The resulting C-terminal Air2p fragment contained a [His]6 tag fusion on its C-terminus. The protein was expressed in LB medium according to the manufacturer (Novagen) and affinity purified on Ni2+-NTA agarose (Sigma) under denaturing conditions as described [5]. After further purification on reverse phase chromatography (GE Healthcare) in FPLC, approximately 100 microg of the purified protein was used for three injections into a rabbit (Eurogentec). Peroxidase-conjugated swine anti-rabbit antibodies (DAKO) served as secondary antibodies for detection of the primary antibodies with the ECL Plus Western blotting detection system (Amersham).
###end p 97
###begin title 98
Telomere Length Analysis
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 68 72 68 72 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000555-Askree1">[44]</xref>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 498 530 498 530 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-TGTGGGTGTGGTGTGTGGGTGTGGTG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 565 567 561 563 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 655 656 651 652 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 659 660 655 656 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 845 848 837 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 931 933 919 921 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 104 109 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Telomere length measurement was carried out as previously described [44]. Genomic DNA was prepared from yeast cells grown in YPD and according to standard procedures. DNA from each strain was digested overnight with the restriction enzyme XhoI and fractionated by 1% agarose gel electrophoresis in 1x TBE buffer (90 mM Tris-borate, 2 mM EDTA) at 40 Volts for 15 h. DNA was transferred to a Hybond-N+ membrane (Amersham) and Southern blot was performed by hybridization with a telomeric probe (26G; 5'-TGTGGGTGTGGTGTGTGGGTGTGGTG-3') that was end-labeled with gamma-[32P] ATP and T4 polynucleotide kinase (Biolabs). All hybridizations were done in 200 mM Na2HPO4, 1 mM EDTA, 2% SDS, 1% BSA and 50 microg/ml salmon sperm DNA. The average telomeric length for each lane was estimated by a 1 kb DNA ladder (peqLab) that was run in a lane next to the XhoI digested genomic DNA. The ladder was probed with the same DNA ladder after gamma-32P end-labeling.
###end p 99
###begin title 100
Supporting Information
###end title 100
###begin p 101
###xml 35 44 35 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 46 55 42 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 61 80 53 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 191 200 179 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 210 219 194 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 233 252 213 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>
###xml 381 394 357 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 381 394 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
Classes of RNAs that accumulate in trf4Delta, trf5Delta, and trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA mutants. Pie chart classifying the transcripts with more than 2-fold (FDRs<5%) increased expression in in the trf4Delta (A), the trf5Delta (B), and the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA (C) mutant strains as determined by microarray analysis. Microarrays contained 10,944 oligo probes (70-mers) representing 6,388 S. cerevisiae ORFs and 3,456 probes to detect ncRNAs (e.g. snRNAs/snoRNAs), rRNA precursors, INTs, Ty1 retrotransposon elements, exon-intron and exon-exon junctions, and 242 IGRs/CUTs. We infer that the fraction of CUTs and ncRNAs in the three mutants is underestimated as our microarrays do not fully cover all the genome's intergenic regions (including both strands) as well as antisense RNAs.

Expression profiles of SnoRNAs and IGRs (CUTs) in RNA surveillance mutants. Microarray analysis of trf4Delta, trf5Delta, and trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA (DADA) mutants showing relative changes for a sample of snoRNAs (14 out of 27; SNR) and IGRs/CUTs the steady-state levels of which were >2-fold increased (FDRs<5%) in trf4Delta mutant cells. snoRNAs and IGRs/CUTs strongly accumulated in the trf4Delta mutant, but not in the trf5Delta mutant. Microarrays are the same as shown in Figure 1.

###begin p 107
###xml 47 56 47 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>

###xml 252 261 244 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf5&#916;</italic>
###xml 270 289 258 273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>

###xml 485 494 469 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 540 548 520 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 674 683 654 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 685 704 661 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;/TRF4-DADA</italic>

###xml 721 730 689 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrp6&#916;</italic>
###xml 911 925 871 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">anti-sense-Ty1</italic>
###xml 927 930 887 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RTL</italic>
###xml 1073 1076 1025 1028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RTL</italic>
###xml 1204 1209 1156 1161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TyA/B</italic>
###xml 1358 1367 1310 1315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1413 1417 1361 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACT1</italic>
###xml 1513 1514 1461 1462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1649 1658 1597 1606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000555-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
Retrotransposon Ty1 elements accumulate in the trf4Delta Mutant and are restored to wt levels by Trf4p-DADA overexpression. (A) Bar diagram representing relative changes of Ty1 retrotransposon RNAs as found by microarray analysis of the trf4Delta, the trf5Delta and the trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA (DADA) mutants. The values are averages of the levels of Ty1 retrotransposon transcripts as displayed by 68 out of 96 Ty1 retrotransposon probes showing more than 2-fold increase (FDR<5%) in the trf4Delta mutant. Microarrays are the same as shown in Figure 1. (B) Bar diagrams show the results of the qRT-PCR analysis for the Ty1 retrotransposon elements in RNA surveillance mutants (trf4Delta, trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta). The scheme above the bar diagram represents the Ty1 retrotransposon locus: grey arrow (UP) indicates the position of the UP-alphaTy1 primer used for strand specific synthesis of anti-sense-Ty1 (RTL) cDNA; convergent solid arrows (alphaTyF and alphaTyR) indicate the primer pairs anti-Ty-Fw and anti-Ty-Rv used for the quantification of the RTL cDNA; convergent grey arrowheads (TyF and TyR) show the location of Ty-Fw and Ty-Rv primers used for the quantification of the TyA/B cDNA. Consistent with the microarray analysis the expression of Ty1 retrotransposon is restored to WT levels by the overexpression of Trf4p-DADA in trf4Delta mutant cells. RNA amounts were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and are compared to the isogenic WT strain. Relative changes of transcript abundances (log2 ratio scale) represent averages from two independent qRT-PCR analyses. The RNA was also used for the microarray analysis presented in Figure 1A.

Intron expression profiles in RNA surveillance mutants. Bar diagrams show the results of qRT-PCR analysis for a group of introns (RPS9A-INT; RPL16A-INT, RPL7B-INT1, GCR1-INT, and RPL40A-INT) in RNA surveillance mutants (trf4Delta, trf4Delta/TRF4-DADA, trf5Delta, and rrp6Delta). qRT-PCR analysis was performed with intron-specific primers. Overexpression of Trf4p-DADA in trf4Delta mutant cells abolished the accumulation of the first intron of RPL7B (RPL7B-INT1) and of GCR1 (GCR1-INT) and reduced by 3.6-fold (log2) the abundance of the intron of RPS9A (RPS9A-INT). RNA amounts were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and are compared relative to the isogenic wild-type strain. Relative changes of transcript abundances (log2 ratio scale) represent averages from two independent qRT-PCR analyses. The RNA was also used for the microarray analysis presented in Figure 1A.

Both HMLalpha1 and ARS318 RNAs strongly accumulated in the rrp6Delta mutant strain. RNA levels were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and compared to the relative expression in isogenic wild-type strain. RNA amounts were normalized to ACT1 mRNA and are compared relative to the isogenic WT strain.
